# nb Â· command line and local web plain text note-taking, bookmarking, archiving, and knowledge base application (xwmx.github.io)

<https://xwmx.github.io/nb/#import>

## Description

A CLI and local web plain text note-taking, bookmarking, archiving, and knowledge base application.

[![Build Status](https://img.shields.io/github/actions/workflow/status/xwmx/nb/tests.yml?branch=master){style="max-width:100%;"}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/actions){rel="nofollow"}

Â 

\

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is a command line and local web noteâ€‘taking, bookmarking, archiving, and knowledge base application with:

-   plain text data storage,
-   [encryption](#password-protected-encrypted-notes-and-bookmarks),
-   [filtering](#listing--filtering), [pinning](#-pinning), [#tagging](#-tagging), and [search](#-search),
-   [Git](https://git-scm.com/)-backed [versioning](#-revision-history) and [syncing](#-git-sync),
-   [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/)-backed [conversion](#%EF%B8%8F-import--export),
-   [\[\[wiki-style linking\]\]](#-linking),
-   terminal and GUI web [browsing](#-browsing),
-   inline [images](#-images),
-   [todos](#-todos) with [tasks](#%EF%B8%8F-tasks),
-   global and local [notebooks](#-notebooks),
-   organization with [folders](#-folders),
-   customizable [color themes](#-color-themes),
-   extensibility through [plugins](#-plugins),

and more, in a single portable script.

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} creates notes in text-based formats like [Markdown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown), [Org](https://orgmode.org/), [LaTeX](https://www.latex-project.org/), and [AsciiDoc](https://asciidoc.org/), can work with files in any format, can import and export notes to many document formats, and can create private, password-protected encrypted notes and bookmarks. With `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, you can write notes using Vim, Emacs, VS Code, Sublime Text, and any other text editor you like, as well as terminal and GUI web browsers. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} works in any standard Linux / Unix environment, including macOS and Windows via WSL. [Optional dependencies](#optional) can be installed to enhance functionality, but `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} works great without them.

![home](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-theme-nb-home.png){width="450"}

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is also a powerful [bookmarking](#-bookmarks) system featuring:

-   locally-served, text-centric, distraction-free bookmark [browsing](#-browsing) in terminal and GUI web browsers,
-   local full-text search of cached page content with regular expression support,
-   convenient filtering and listing,
-   [Internet Archive Wayback Machine](https://archive.org/web/) snapshot lookup for broken links,
-   tagging, pinning, linking, and full integration with other `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} features.

Page information is downloaded, cleaned up, structured, and saved into normal Markdown documents made for humans, so bookmarks are easy to view and edit just like any other note.

![nb browse](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/gui-terminal-browse.png){width="500"}

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} uses [Git](https://git-scm.com/) in the background to automatically record changes and sync notebooks with remote repositories. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can also be configured to sync notebooks using a general purpose syncing utility like Dropbox so notes can be edited in other apps on any device.

![nb list empty](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/terminal-empty.png){width="450"}

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is designed to be portable, future-focused, and vendor independent, providing a full-featured and intuitive experience within a highly composable multimodal user-centric text interface. The entire program is contained within a single [well-tested](#tests) shell script that can be installed, copied, or `curl`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}ed almost anywhere and just work, using a strategy inspired by [progressive enhancement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_enhancement) for various experience improvements in more capable environments. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} works great whether you have one notebook with just a few notes or dozens of notebooks containing thousands of notes, bookmarks, and other items. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} makes it easy to incorporate other tools, writing apps, and workflows. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can be used a little, a lot, once in a while, or for just a subset of features. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is flexible.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#installation){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="installation"} Installation

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#dependencies){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="dependencies"} Dependencies

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#required){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="required"} Required

-   [Bash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bash_(Unix_shell))
    -   `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} works perfectly with Zsh, fish, and any other shell set as your primary login shell, the system just needs to have Bash available on it.
-   [Git](https://git-scm.com/)
-   A text editor with command line support, such as:
    -   [Vim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vim_\(text_editor\)),
    -   [Emacs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emacs),
    -   [Visual Studio Code](https://code.visualstudio.com/),
    -   [Sublime Text](https://www.sublimetext.com/),
    -   [micro](https://github.com/zyedidia/micro),
    -   [nano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GNU_nano),
    -   [Atom](https://atom.io/),
    -   [TextMate](https://macromates.com/),
    -   [MacDown](https://macdown.uranusjr.com/),
    -   [some of these](https://github.com/topics/text-editor),
    -   [and many of these.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_text_editors)

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#optional){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="optional"} Optional

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} leverages standard command line tools and works in standard Linux / Unix environments. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also checks the environment for some additional optional tools and uses them to enhance the experience whenever they are available.

Recommended:

-   [`bat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/sharkdp/bat)
-   [`ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://nmap.org/ncat/)
-   [`pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://pandoc.org/)
-   [`rg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/BurntSushi/ripgrep)
-   [`tig`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/jonas/tig)
-   [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m)

Also supported for various enhancements:

[Ack](https://beyondgrep.com/), [`afplay`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://ss64.com/osx/afplay.html), [`asciidoctor`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://asciidoctor.org/), [The Silver Searcher (`ag`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge})](https://github.com/ggreer/the_silver_searcher), [`catimg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/posva/catimg), [Chafa](https://github.com/hpjansson/chafa), [`exa`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/ogham/exa), [`ffplay`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://ffmpeg.org/ffplay.html), [ImageMagick](https://imagemagick.org/), [GnuPG](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GNU_Privacy_Guard), [`highlight`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](http://www.andre-simon.de/doku/highlight/en/highlight.php), [`imgcat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://www.iterm2.com/documentation-images.html), [`joshuto`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/kamiyaa/joshuto), [kitty's `icat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} kitten](https://sw.kovidgoyal.net/kitty/kittens/icat.html), [Links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)), [Lynx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynx_(web_browser)), [Midnight Commander (`mc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge})](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midnight_Commander), [`mpg123`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mpg123), [MPlayer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MPlayer), [ncat](https://nmap.org/ncat/), [note-link-janitor](https://github.com/andymatuschak/note-link-janitor) (via [plugin](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/backlink.nb-plugin)), [`pdftotext`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pdftotext), [Pygments](https://pygments.org/), [Ranger](https://ranger.github.io/), [readability-cli](https://gitlab.com/gardenappl/readability-cli), [`rga`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} / ripgrep-all](https://github.com/phiresky/ripgrep-all), [`sc-im`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/andmarti1424/sc-im), [`term-image`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/AnonymouX47/term-image), [`termpdf.py`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/dsanson/termpdf.py), [Tidy-Viewer (`tv`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge})](https://github.com/alexhallam/tv), [`timg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/hzeller/timg), [vifm](https://vifm.info/), [`viu`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/atanunq/viu), [VisiData](https://www.visidata.org/)

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#macos--homebrew){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="macos--homebrew"} macOS / Homebrew {#macos--homebrew}

``` highlight
brew install xwmx/taps/nb
```

Installing `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} with Homebrew also installs the recommended dependencies above and completion scripts for Bash, Zsh, and Fish.

Install the latest development version from the respository with:

``` highlight
brew install xwmx/taps/nb --head
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is also available in [homebrew-core](https://github.com/Homebrew/homebrew-core). Installing it together with the `bash`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} formula is recommended:

``` highlight
brew install nb bash
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#ubuntu-windows-wsl-and-others){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="ubuntu-windows-wsl-and-others"} Ubuntu, Windows WSL, and others

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#npm){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="npm"} npm

``` highlight
npm install -g nb.sh
```

After `npm`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} installation completes, run `sudo "$(which nb)" completions install`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to install Bash and Zsh completion scripts (recommended).

On Ubuntu and WSL, you can run [`sudo "$(which nb)" env install`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#env) to install the optional dependencies.

*`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is also available under its original package name, [notes.sh](https://www.npmjs.com/package/notes.sh), which comes with an extra `notes`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} executable wrapping `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}.*

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#download-and-install){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="download-and-install"} Download and Install

To install as an administrator, copy and paste one of the following multi-line commands:

``` highlight
# install using wget
sudo wget https://raw.github.com/xwmx/nb/master/nb -O /usr/local/bin/nb &&
  sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/nb &&
  sudo nb completions install

# install using curl
sudo curl -L https://raw.github.com/xwmx/nb/master/nb -o /usr/local/bin/nb &&
  sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/nb &&
  sudo nb completions install
```

On Ubuntu and WSL, you can run [`sudo nb env install`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#env) to install the optional dependencies.

###### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#user-only-installation){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="user-only-installation"} User-only Installation

To install with just user permissions, simply add the `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} script to your `$PATH`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}. If you already have a `~/bin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} directory, for example, you can use one of the following commands:

``` highlight
# download with wget
wget https://raw.github.com/xwmx/nb/master/nb -O ~/bin/nb && chmod +x ~/bin/nb

# download with curl
curl -L https://raw.github.com/xwmx/nb/master/nb -o ~/bin/nb && chmod +x ~/bin/nb
```

Installing with just user permissions doesn't include the optional dependencies or completions, but `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} core functionality works without them. If you have `sudo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} access and want to install the completion scripts and dependencies, run the following command:

``` highlight
sudo nb env install
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#make){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="make"} Make

To install with [Make](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Make_(software)), clone this repository, navigate to the clone's root directory, and run:

``` highlight
sudo make install
```

This will also install the completion scripts on all systems and the recommended dependencies on Ubuntu and WSL.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#bpkg){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="bpkg"} bpkg

To install with [bpkg](https://github.com/bpkg/bpkg):

``` highlight
bpkg install xwmx/nb
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#basher){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="basher"} basher

To install with [basher](https://www.basher.it/):

``` highlight
basher install xwmx/nb
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#tab-completion){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="tab-completion"} Tab Completion

Bash, Fish, and Zsh tab completion should be enabled when `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is installed using the methods above, assuming you have the appropriate system permissions or installed with `sudo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}. If completion isn't working after installing `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, see the [completion installation instructions](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/tree/master/etc).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#updating){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="updating"} Updating

When `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is installed using a package manager like npm or Homebrew, use the package manager's upgrade functionality to update `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to the latest version. When installed via other methods, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can be updated to the latest version using the [`nb update`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#update) subcommand.

## [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#overview){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="overview"} Overview

[`ğŸ“`Â Notes](#-notes)Â Â· [Adding](#adding)Â Â· [Listing](#listing--filtering)Â Â· [Editing](#editing)Â Â· [Viewing](#viewing)Â Â· [Deleting](#deleting)Â Â· [`ğŸ”–`Â Bookmarks](#-bookmarks)Â Â· [`âœ…`Â Todos](#-todos)Â Â· [`âœ”ï¸`Â Tasks](#%EF%B8%8F-tasks)Â Â· [`ğŸ·`Â Tagging](#-tagging)Â Â· [`ğŸ”—`Â Linking](#-linking)Â Â· [`ğŸŒ`Â Browsing](#-browsing)Â Â· [`ğŸŒ„`Â Images](#-images)Â Â· [`ğŸ—‚`Â Zettelkasten](#-zettelkasten)Â Â· [`ğŸ“‚`Â Folders](#-folders)Â Â· [`ğŸ“Œ`Â Pinning](#-pinning)Â Â· [`ğŸ”`Â Search](#-search)Â Â· [`â†”`Â MovingÂ &Â Renaming](#-moving--renaming)Â Â· [`ğŸ—’`Â History](#-revision-history)Â Â· [`ğŸ“š`Â Notebooks](#-notebooks)Â Â· [`ğŸ”„`Â GitÂ Sync](#-git-sync)Â Â· [`â†•ï¸`Â ImportÂ /Â Export](#%EF%B8%8F-import--export)Â Â· [`âš™ï¸``set`&`settings`](#%EF%B8%8F-set--settings)Â Â· [`ğŸ¨`Â ColorÂ Themes](#-color-themes)Â Â· [`ğŸ”Œ`Â Plugins](#-plugins)Â Â· [`:/`Â Selectors](#-selectors)Â Â· [`01`Â Metadata](#01-metadata)Â Â· [`â¯`Â Shell](#-interactive-shell)Â Â· [Shortcuts](#shortcut-aliases)Â Â· [`?`Â Help](#-help)Â Â· [`$`Â Variables](#-variables)Â Â· [Specifications](#specifications)Â Â· [Tests](#tests)

[Â â†‘Â ](#nb)

To get started, simply run:

``` highlight
nb
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} sets up your initial `home`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} notebook the first time it runs.

By default, notebooks and notes are global (at `~/.nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}), so they are always available to `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} regardless of the current working directory. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also supports [local notebooks](#global-and-local-notebooks).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-notes){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-notes"} ğŸ“ Notes {#-notes}

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#adding){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="adding"} Adding

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb add`](#add),\ [`nb browse add`](#browse)^

Use [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) (shortcuts: [`nb a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`nb +`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add)) to create new notes:

``` highlight
# create a new note in your text editor
nb add

# create a new note with the filename "example.md"
nb add example.md

# create a new note containing "This is a note."
nb add "This is a note."

# create a new note with piped content
echo "Note content." | nb add

# create a new password-protected, encrypted note titled "Secret Document"
nb add --title "Secret Document" --encrypt

# create a new note in the notebook named "example"
nb example:add "This is a note."

# create a new note in the folder named "sample"
nb add sample/
```

[`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) with no arguments or input will open the new, blank note in your environment's preferred text editor. You can change your editor using the `$EDITOR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} environment variable or [`nb set editor`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#editor).

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files are [Markdown](https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/) files by default. The default file type can be changed to whatever you like using [`nb set default_extension`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#default_extension).

[`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) has intelligent argument parsing and behaves differently depending on the types of arguments it receives. When a filename with extension is specified, a new note with that filename is opened in the editor:

``` highlight
nb add example.md
```

When a string is specified, a new note is immediately created with that string as the content and without opening the editor:

``` highlight
â¯ nb add "This is a note."
Added: [1] 20200101000000.md
```

[`nb add <string>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) is useful for quickly jotting down notes directly via the command line. Quoting content is optional, but recommended.

When no filename is specified, [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) uses the current datetime as the filename.

[`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) can also receive piped content, which behaves the same as [`nb add <string>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add):

``` highlight
# create a new note containing "Note content."
â¯ echo "Note content." | nb add
Added: [6] 20200101000100.md

# create a new note containing the clipboard contents on macOS
â¯ pbpaste | nb add
Added: [7] 20200101000200.md

# create a new note containing the clipboard contents using xclip
â¯ xclip -o | nb add
Added: [8] 20200101000300.md
```

Content can be passed with the [`--content <content>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) option, which also creates a new note without opening the editor:

``` highlight
nb add --content "Note content."
```

When content is piped, specified with [`--content <content>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), or passed as a string argument, use the [`--edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) flag to open the file in the editor before the change is committed.

The title, filename, and content can also be specified with long and short options:

``` highlight
â¯ nb add --filename "example.md" -t "Example Title" -c "Example content."
Added: [9] example.md "Example Title"
```

The [`-t <title>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) / [`--title <title>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) option also sets the filename to the title, lowercased with spaces and non-filename characters replaced with underscores:

``` highlight
â¯ nb add --title "Example Title" "Example content."
Added: [10] example_title.md "Example Title"
```

Tags can be added with the [`--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) option, which takes a comma separated list of tags, converts them to [#hashtags](#-tagging), and inserts them between the title and content:

``` highlight
â¯ nb add "Example content." --title "Tagged Example" --tags tag1,tag2
Added: [11] tagged_example.md "Tagged Example"

â¯ nb show 11 --print
# Tagged Example

#tag1 #tag2

Example content.
```

[Search](#-search) for tagged items with [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search):

``` highlight
# search for items tagged with "#tag1"
nb search --tag tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2", short options
nb q -t tag1 -t tag2

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2", arguments
nb q \#tag1 --or \#tag2
```

Files can be created with any file type by specifying the extension either in the filename (`example.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}), the extension by itself (`.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}), or via the [`--type <type>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) option (`--type md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}):

``` highlight
# open a new Org file in the editor
nb add example.org

# open a new reStructuredText file in the editor
nb add --type rst

# open a new JavaScript file in the editor
nb add .js
```

Combining a type argument with piped clipboard content provides a very convenient way to save code snippets using a clipboard utility such as `pbpaste`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `xclip`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, or [`pb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/pb):

``` highlight
# save the clipboard contents as a JavaScript file in the current notebook
pb | nb add .js

# save the clipboard contents as a Rust file in the "rust" notebook
# using the shortcut alias `nb a`
pb | nb a rust: .rs

# save the clipboard contents as a Haskell file named "example.hs" in the
# "snippets" notebook using the shortcut alias `nb +`
pb | nb + snippets: example.hs
```

Use [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) and [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) to view code snippets with automatic syntax highlighting and use [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) to open in your editor.

The [`clip`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} plugin](#clip) can also be used to create notes from clipboard content.

Piping, [`--title <title>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`--tags <tag-list>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`--content <content>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), and content passed in an argument can be combined as needed to create notes with content from multiple input methods and sources using a single command:

``` highlight
â¯ pb | nb add "Argument content." \
    --title   "Sample Title"      \
    --tags    tag1,tag2           \
    --content "Option content."
Added: [12] sample_title.md "Sample Title"

â¯ nb show 12 --print
# Sample Title

#tag1 #tag2

Argument content.

Option content.

Clipboard content.
```

For a full list of options available for [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), run [`nb help add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#password-protected-encrypted-notes-and-bookmarks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="password-protected-encrypted-notes-and-bookmarks"} Password-Protected Encrypted Notes and Bookmarks

Password-protected notes and [bookmarks](#-bookmarks) are created with the [`-e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) / [`--encrypt`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) flag and encrypted with AES-256 using OpenSSL by default. GPG is also supported and can be configured with [`nb set encryption_tool`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#encryption_tool).

Each protected note and bookmark is encrypted individually with its own password. When an encrypted item is viewed, edited, or opened, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} will simply prompt for the item's password before proceeding. After an item is edited, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} automatically re-encrypts it and saves the new version.

Encrypted notes can be decrypted using the OpenSSL and GPG command line tools directly, so you aren't dependent on `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to decrypt your files.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-aliases-nb-a-nb-){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-aliases-nb-a-nb-"} Shortcut Aliases: `nb a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `nb +`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} {#shortcut-aliases-nb-a-nb-}

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes shortcuts for many commands, including [`nb a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) and [`nb +`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) for [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add):

``` highlight
# create a new note in your text editor
nb a

# create a new note with the filename "example.md"
nb a example.md

# create a new note containing "This is a note."
nb + "This is a note."

# create a new note containing the clipboard contents with xclip
xclip -o | nb +

# create a new note in the notebook named "example"
nb example:a
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#other-aliases-nb-create-nb-new){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="other-aliases-nb-create-nb-new"} Other Aliases: `nb create`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `nb new`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) can also be invoked with [`nb create`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) and [`nb new`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) for convenience:

``` highlight
# create a new note containing "Example note content."
nb new "Example note content."

# create a new note with the title "Example Note Title"
nb create --title "Example Note Title"
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#adding-with-nb-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="adding-with-nb-browse"} Adding with `nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can also be added within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse add
â¯nb Â· home : +

[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]

[add]
```

Pass a filename, relative path, and / or notebook name to create a new note at that location:

``` highlight
# open the add form in the browser to create the file "file.md" in the folder "example"
nb browse add "example/file.md"
```

[`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) includes options for quickly pre-populating new notes with content:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse add --title "Example Title" --content "Example content." --tags tag1,tag2
â¯nb Â· home : +

[# Example Title                                      ]
[                                                     ]
[#tag1 #tag2                                          ]
[                                                     ]
[Example content.                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]
[                                                     ]

[add]
```

[`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) can also be opened with [`nb add --browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) / [`nb a -b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add).

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#listing--filtering){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="listing--filtering"} Listing & Filtering {#listing--filtering}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb ls`](#ls),\ [`nb list`](#list),\ [`nb browse`](#browse)^

To list notes and notebooks, run [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) (shortcut alias: `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}):

![nb ls](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-theme-utility-home.png){width="450"}

Notebooks are listed above the line, with the current notebook highlighted and/or underlined, depending on terminal capabilities. [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) also includes a footer with example commands for easy reference. The notebook header and command footer can be configured or hidden with [`nb set header`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#header) and [`nb set footer`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#footer).

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls
home
----
[3] example.md Â· "Example content."
[2] sample.md Â· "Sample content."
[1] demo.md Â· "- Demo list item one."
```

Notes from the current notebook are listed in the order they were last modified. By default, each note is listed with its id, filename, and an excerpt from the first line of the note. When a note has a title, the title is displayed instead of the filename and first line.

Markdown titles can be defined within a note using [either Markdown `h1`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} style](https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/syntax#header) or [YAML front matter](#front-matter):

``` highlight
# Example Title
```

``` highlight
Sample Title
============
```

``` highlight
---
title: Demo Title
---
```

[Org](https://orgmode.org/), [LaTeX](https://www.latex-project.org/), and [AsciiDoc](https://asciidoc.org/) titles are recognized in `.org`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge},`.latex`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, and `.asciidoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} / `.adoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files:

``` highlight
#+TITLE: Example Org Title
```

``` highlight
\title{Example LaTeX Title}
```

``` asciidoc
= Example AsciiDoc Title
```

Once defined, titles are displayed in place of the filename and first line in the output of [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls):

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls
home
----
[3] Example Title
[2] Sample Title
[1] Demo Title
```

Pass an id, filename, or title to view the listing for that note:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls Sample\ Title
[2] Sample Title

â¯ nb ls 3
[3] Example Title
```

If there is no exact match, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} will list items with titles and filenames that fuzzy match the query:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls exa
[3] Example Title

â¯ nb ls ample
[3] Example Title
[2] Sample Title
```

Multiple words act like an `OR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} filter, listing any titles or filenames that match any of the words:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls example demo
[3] Example Title
[1] Demo Title
```

When multiple words are quoted, filter titles and filenames for that phrase:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls "example title"
[3] Example Title
```

For full text search, see [Search](#-search).

To view excerpts of notes, use the [`--excerpt`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) or [`-e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) option, which optionally accepts a length:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls 3 --excerpt
[3] Example Title
-----------------
# Example Title

This is an example excerpt.

â¯ nb ls 3 -e 8
[3] Example Title
-----------------
# Example Title

This is an example excerpt.

More example content:

- one
- two
```

Several classes of file types are represented with emoji [indicators](#indicators) to make them easily identifiable in lists. For example, bookmarks and encrypted notes are listed with `ğŸ”–`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `ğŸ”’`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls
home
----
[4] Example Note
[3] ğŸ”’ encrypted-note.md.enc
[2] ğŸ”– Example Bookmark (example.com)
[1] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
```

File types include:

``` highlight
 ğŸ”‰  Audio
 ğŸ“–  Book
 ğŸ”–  Bookmark
 ğŸ”’  Encrypted
 ğŸ“‚  Folder
 ğŸŒ„  Image
 ğŸ“„  PDF, Word, or Open Office document
 ğŸ“¹  Video
```

By default, items are listed starting with the most recently modified. To reverse the order, use the [`-r`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) or [`--reverse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) flag:

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls
home
----
[2] Todos
[3] Example Title
[1] Ideas

â¯ nb ls --reverse
[1] Ideas
[3] Example Title
[2] Todos
```

Notes can be sorted with the [`-s`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`--sort`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) flag, which can be combined with [`-r`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`--reverse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls):

``` highlight
â¯ nb ls
home
----
[2] Sample Title
[3] Example Title
[1] Demo Title

â¯ nb ls --sort
[1] Demo Title
[2] Sample Title
[3] Example Title

â¯ nb ls --sort --reverse
[3] Example Title
[2] Sample Title
[1] Demo Title
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} with no subcommand behaves like an alias for [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), so the examples above can be run without the `ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[2] Sample Title
[3] Example Title
[1] Demo Title

â¯ nb example
[3] Example Title

â¯ nb 3 --excerpt
[3] Example Title
-----------------
# Example Title

This is an example excerpt.

â¯ nb 3 -e 8
[3] Example Title
-----------------
# Example Title

This is an example excerpt.

More example content:

- one
- two

â¯ nb --sort
[1] Demo Title
[2] Sample Title
[3] Example Title

â¯ nb --sort --reverse
[3] Example Title
[2] Sample Title
[1] Demo Title
```

Short options can be combined for brevity:

``` highlight
# equivalent to `nb --sort --reverse --excerpt 2` and `nb -s -r -e 2`:
â¯ nb -sre 2
[3] Example Title
-----------------
# Example Title

[2] Sample Title
----------------
Sample Title
============
[1] Demo Title
--------------
---
title: Demo Title
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) display the 15 most recently modified items. The default limit can be changed with [`nb set limit <number>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#limit). To list a different number of items on a per-command basis, use the [`-n <limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`--limit <limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`--<limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`-a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), and [`--all`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) flags:

``` highlight
â¯ nb -n 1
home
----
[5] Example Five
4 omitted. 5 total.

â¯ nb --limit 2
home
----
[5] Example Five
[4] Example Four
3 omitted. 5 total.

â¯ nb --3
home
----
[5] Example Five
[4] Example Four
[3] Example Three
2 omitted. 5 total.

â¯ nb --all
home
----
[5] Example Five
[4] Example Four
[3] Example Three
[2] Example Two
[1] Example One
```

Lists can be paginated with [`-p <number>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`--page <number>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), which paginates by the value of [`nb set limit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#limit) by default, or the value of [`-n <limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`--limit <limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), or [`--<limit>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) when present:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[6] Example Six
[5] Example Five
[4] Example Four
[3] Example Three
[2] Example Two
[1] Example One

â¯ nb set limit 3
NB_LIMIT set to 3

â¯ nb --page 1
[6] Example Six
[5] Example Five
[4] Example Four

â¯ nb -p 2
[3] Example Three
[2] Example Two
[1] Example One

â¯ nb -p 2 --limit 2
[4] Example Four
[3] Example Three

â¯ nb -p 3 --2
[2] Example Two
[1] Example One
```

List [#tagged](#tagging) items by passing `\#escaped`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or `"#quoted"`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} hashtags or tags specified with the [`--tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) option. Multiple tags perform an `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} query:

``` highlight
# list items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1", escaped
nb \#tag1

# list items in the "example" notebook tagged with "#tag2", quoted
nb example: "#tag2"

# list items in all notebooks tagged with "#tag1", long option
nb \#tag1 --all

# list items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb \#tag1 "#tag2"

# list items in all notebooks tagged with "#tag2" AND "#tag3", short option
nb --tags tag2,tag3 -a
```

[`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) is a combination of [`nb notebooks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) and [`nb list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list) in one view and accepts the same arguments as [`nb list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list), which lists only notes without the notebook list and with no limit by default:

``` highlight
â¯ nb list
[100] Example One Hundred
[99]  Example Ninety-Nine
[98]  Example Ninety-Eight
... lists all notes ...
[2]   Example Two
[1]   Example One
```

For more information about options for listing notes, run [`nb help ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) and [`nb help list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#listing-with-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="listing-with-browse"} Listing with `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can be listed within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse example:sample/demo/
â¯nb Â· example : sample / demo / +

search: [                    ]

[example:sample/demo/7] Title Seven
[example:sample/demo/6] Title Six
[example:sample/demo/5] Title Five
[example:sample/demo/4] Title Four
[example:sample/demo/3] Title Three

next â¯
```

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#editing){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="editing"} Editing

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb edit`](#edit),\ [`nb browse edit`](#browse)^

You can edit an item in your editor with [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) (shortcut: [`nb e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit)):

``` highlight
# edit note by id
nb edit 3

# edit note by filename
nb edit example.md

# edit note by title
nb edit "A Document Title"

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb edit example:12

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 edit

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:edit 12
```

[`edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) and other subcommands that take an identifier can be called with the identifier and subcommand name reversed:

``` highlight
# edit note by id
nb 3 edit
```

[`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) can also receive piped content, which it appends to the specified note without opening the editor:

``` highlight
echo "Content to append." | nb edit 1
```

Content can be passed with the [`--content <content>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) option, which also appends the content without opening the editor:

``` highlight
nb edit 1 --content "Content to append."
```

Use the [`--overwrite`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) option to overwrite existing file content and the [`--prepend`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) option to prepend the new content before existing content.

When content is piped or specified with [`--content <content>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit), use the [`--edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) flag to open the file in the editor before the change is committed.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#editing-encrypted-notes){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="editing-encrypted-notes"} Editing Encrypted Notes

When a note is encrypted, [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) prompts you for the note password, opens the unencrypted content in your editor, and then automatically reencrypts the note when you are done editing.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-alias-nb-e){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-alias-nb-e"} Shortcut Alias: `nb e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) can be called by the shortcut alias, [`nb e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit):

``` highlight
# edit note by id
nb e 3

# edit note by filename
nb e example.md

# edit note by title
nb e "A Document Title"

# edit note by id, alternative
nb 3 e

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb e example:12

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 e

# edit note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:e 12
```

For [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) help information, run [`nb help edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#editing-with-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="editing-with-browse"} Editing with `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can be edited within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse edit text:formats/markdown/123
â¯nb Â· text : formats / markdown / 123 Â· â†“ Â· editing Â· - | +

[# Daring Fireball: Markdown (daringfireball.net)         ]
[                                                         ]
[<https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/>          ]
[                                                         ]
[## Related                                               ]
[                                                         ]
[- <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown>               ]
[                                                         ]
[## Comments                                              ]
[                                                         ]
[See also:                                                ]
[                                                         ]
[- [[text:formats/org]]                                   ]
[- [[cli:apps/nb]]                                        ]
[                                                         ]
[## Tags                                                  ]
[                                                         ]

[save] Â·Â last: 2021-01-01 01:00:00
```

For more information, see [`browse edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse-edit) and [Browsing](#-browsing).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#viewing){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="viewing"} Viewing

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb show`](#show),\ [`nb browse`](#browse),\ [`nb open`](#open),\ [`nb peek`](#peek)^

Notes and other items can be viewed using [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) (shortcut: [`nb s`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show)):

``` highlight
# show note by id
nb show 3

# show note by filename
nb show example.md

# show note by title
nb show "A Document Title"

# show note by id, alternative
nb 3 show

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb show example:12

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 show

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:show 12
```

By default, [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) opens notes in [`less`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://linux.die.net/man/1/less), with syntax highlighting if [`bat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/sharkdp/bat), [`highlight`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](http://www.andre-simon.de/doku/highlight/en/highlight.php), or [Pygments](https://pygments.org/) is installed. You can navigate in `less`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} using the following keys:

``` highlight
Key               Function
---               --------
mouse scroll      Scroll up or down
arrow up or down  Scroll one line up or down
f                 Jump forward one window
b                 Jump back one window
d                 Jump down one half window
u                 Jump up one half window
/<query>          Search for <query>
n                 Jump to next <query> match
q                 Quit
```

*If `less`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} scrolling isn't working in [iTerm2](https://www.iterm2.com/), go to* "Settings" -\> "Advanced" -\> "Scroll wheel sends arrow keys when in alternate screen mode" *and change it to* "Yes". *[More Info](https://stackoverflow.com/a/37610820)*

Use the [`-p`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`--print`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) option to print to standard output with syntax highlighting:

``` highlight
â¯ nb show 123 --print
# Example Title

Example content:

- one
- two
- three
```

Use [`nb show --print --no-color`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) to print without syntax highlighting.

When [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/) is available, use the [`-r`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`--render`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) option to render the note to HTML and open it in your terminal browser:

``` highlight
nb show example.md --render
# opens example.md as an HTML page in w3m, links, or lynx
```

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) also supports previewing other file types in the terminal, depending on the tools available in the environment. To prefer specific tools for certain file types, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} provides configuration variables that can be set in your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file, which can be opened in your editor with [`nb settings edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings).

Supported file types and tools include:

-   PDF files:
    -   [`termpdf.py`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/dsanson/termpdf.py) with [kitty](https://sw.kovidgoyal.net/kitty/)
    -   [`pdftotext`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pdftotext)
-   Audio files ([`$NB_AUDIO_TOOL`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_audio_tool)):
    -   [`mplayer`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MPlayer)
    -   [`afplay`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://ss64.com/osx/afplay.html)
    -   [`mpg123`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mpg123)
    -   [`ffplay`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://ffmpeg.org/ffplay.html)
-   [Images](#-images) ([`$NB_IMAGE_TOOL`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_image_tool)):
    -   [`catimg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/posva/catimg)
    -   [Chafa](https://github.com/hpjansson/chafa)
    -   [ImageMagick](https://imagemagick.org/) with a terminal that supports [sixels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sixel)
    -   [`imgcat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://www.iterm2.com/documentation-images.html) with [iTerm2](https://www.iterm2.com/)
    -   [kitty's `icat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} kitten](https://sw.kovidgoyal.net/kitty/kittens/icat.html)
    -   [`term-image`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/AnonymouX47/term-image)
    -   [`timg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/hzeller/timg)
    -   [`viu`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/atanunq/viu)
-   Folders, Directories, Notebooks ([`$NB_DIRECTORY_TOOL`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_directory_tool)):
    -   [`exa`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/ogham/exa)
    -   [`joshuto`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/kamiyaa/joshuto)
    -   [Midnight Commander (`mc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge})](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midnight_Commander)
    -   [`ranger`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://ranger.github.io/)
    -   [`vifm`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://vifm.info/)
-   Word Documents:
    -   [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/) with [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m) or [`links`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser))
-   Excel, CSV, TSV, and data files ([`$NB_DATA_TOOL`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_data_tool)):
    -   [VisiData](https://www.visidata.org/)
    -   [`sc-im`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/andmarti1424/sc-im)
    -   [Tidy-Viewer (`tv`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge})](https://github.com/alexhallam/tv)
-   EPUB ebooks:
    -   [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/) with [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m) or [`links`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser))

When using [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) with other file types or if the above tools are not available, [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) opens files in your system's preferred application for each type.

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) also provides [options](#show) for querying information about an item. For example, use the [`--added`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`-a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) and [`--updated`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`-u`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) flags to print the date and time that an item was added or updated:

``` highlight
â¯ nb show 2 --added
2020-01-01 01:01:00 -0700

â¯ nb show 2 --updated
2020-02-02 02:02:00 -0700
```

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) is primarily intended for viewing items within the terminal. To view a file in the system's preferred GUI application, use [`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open). To [browse](#-browsing) rendered items in terminal and GUI web browsers, use [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

For full [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) usage information, run [`nb help show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-alias-nb-s){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-alias-nb-s"} Shortcut Alias: `nb s`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) can be called using the shortcut alias [`nb s`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show):

``` highlight
# show note by id
nb s 3

# show note by filename
nb s example.md

# show note by title
nb s "A Document Title"

# show note by id, alternative
nb 3 s

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb s example:12

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 s

# show note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:s 12
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#alias-nb-view){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="alias-nb-view"} Alias: `nb view`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) can also be invoked with [`nb view`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) for convenience:

``` highlight
# show note by id
nb view 3

# show note by filename
nb view example.md

# show note by title
nb view "A Document Title"

# show note by id, alternative
nb 3 view
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#viewing-with-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="viewing-with-browse"} Viewing with `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can be viewed within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse text:formats/markdown/123
â¯nb Â· text : formats / markdown / 123 Â· â†“ Â· edit | +
Daring Fireball: Markdown (daringfireball.net)

https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/

Related

  â€¢ https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown

Comments

See also:

  â€¢ [[text:formats/org]]
  â€¢ [[cli:apps/nb]]

Tags

#markup #plain-text

Content

Daring Fireball: Markdown

Download

Markdown 1.0.1 (18 KB)â€‰â€”â€‰17 Dec 2004

Introduction

Markdown is a text-to-HTML conversion tool for web writers. Markdown allows
you to write using an easy-to-read, easy-to-write plain text format, then
convert it to structurally valid XHTML (or HTML).
```

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#deleting){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="deleting"} Deleting

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb delete`](#delete),\ [`nb browse delete`](#browse)^

To delete one or more notes, pass any number of ids, filenames, titles, and other [selectors](#-selectors) to [`nb delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) (shortcuts: [`nb d`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete), [`nb -`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete)):

``` highlight
# delete item by id
nb delete 3

# delete item by filename
nb delete example.md

# delete item by title
nb delete "A Document Title"

# delete item by id, alternative
nb 3 delete

# delete item 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb delete example:12

# delete item 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 delete

# delete item 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:delete 12

# delete item 345 in the folder named "example"
nb delete example/345

# delete items with the ids 89, 56, and 21
nb delete 89 56 21
```

By default, [`nb delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) will display a confirmation prompt. To skip, use the [`--force`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) / [`-f`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) option:

``` highlight
nb delete 3 --force
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-aliases-nb-d-nb--){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-aliases-nb-d-nb--"} Shortcut Aliases: `nb d`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `nb -`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) has the aliases [`nb d`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) and [`nb -`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete):

``` highlight
# delete note by id
nb d 3

# delete note by filename
nb d example.md

# delete note by title
nb - "A Document Title"

# delete note by id, alternative
nb 3 d

# delete note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb - example:12

# delete note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 d

# delete note 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:d 12
```

For [`nb delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete) help information, run [`nb help delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#deleting-with-nb-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="deleting-with-nb-browse"} Deleting with `nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can be deleted within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b d`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse delete example:4
â¯nb Â· example : 4 Â· â†“ Â· edit Â· - | +

              deleting

[4] example_file.md "Example Title"

              [delete]
Â 
```

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-bookmarks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-bookmarks"} ğŸ”– Bookmarks {#-bookmarks}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nbÂ <url>`](#nb-help),\ [`nbÂ browse`](#browse),\ [`nbÂ bookmark`](#bookmark),\ [`nbÂ open`](#open),\ [`nbÂ peek`](#peek),\ [`nbÂ show`](#show)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes a bookmarking system to conveniently create, annotate, view, search, [browse](#-browsing), and manage collections of bookmarks.

![nb bookmarks](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-bookmarks-gui-gui-terminal.png){width="450"}

Bookmarks in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} are stored as [simple structured Markdown files](#nb-markdown-bookmark-file-format) containing information extracted from the bookmarked pages.

To create a new bookmark, pass a URL as the first argument to `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
nb https://example.com
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} automatically generates a bookmark using information from the page:

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} embeds the page content in the bookmark, making it available for [full text search](#-search) with [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) and locally-served, distraction-free [reading and browsing](#-browsing) with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse). When [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/) is installed, the HTML page content is converted to Markdown. When [readability-cli](https://gitlab.com/gardenappl/readability-cli) is installed, markup is cleaned up to focus on content.

In addition to caching the page content, you can also include a quote from the page in a [`## Quote`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-quote) section using the [`-q <quote>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) / [`--quote <quote>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) option:

``` highlight
nb https://example.com --quote "Example quote line one.

Example quote line two."
```

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Quote

> Example quote line one.
>
> Example quote line two.

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

Add a comment in a [`## Comment`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-comment) section using the [`-c <comment>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) / [`--comment <comment>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) option:

``` highlight
nb https://example.com --comment "Example comment."
```

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Comment

Example comment.

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

Add related URLs and [linked](#-linking) [selectors](#-selectors) to a [`## Related`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-related) section using the [`-r (<url> | <selector>)`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) / [`--related (<url> | <selector>)`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) option:

``` highlight
nb https://example.com --related example:123 -r https://example.net
```

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Related

- [[example:123]]
- <https://example.net>

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

Bookmarks can be tagged using the [`-t <tag1>,<tag2>...`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) / [`--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) option. Tags are converted into [#hashtags](#-tagging) and added to a [`## Tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-tags) section:

``` highlight
nb https://example.com --tags tag1,tag2
```

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Tags

#tag1 #tag2

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

[Search](#-search) for tagged bookmarks with [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search):

``` highlight
nb search --tag tag1

nb q -t tag1

nb q \#tag1
```

[`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) automatically searches archived page content:

``` highlight
â¯ nb q "example query"
[10] ğŸ”– example.bookmark.md "Example Bookmark (example.com)"
------------------------------------------------------------
5:Lorem ipsum example query.
```

Bookmarks can also be encrypted:

``` highlight
# create a new password-protected, encrypted bookmark
nb https://example.com --encrypt
```

Encrypted bookmarks require a password before they can be viewed or opened.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#listing-and-filtering-bookmarks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="listing-and-filtering-bookmarks"} Listing and Filtering Bookmarks

![nb bookmark lists](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-bookmarks-gui-terminal-terminal.png){width="500"}

Bookmarks are included in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`nb list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list), and [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) along with items of other types. [`nb bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) and [`nb bookmark list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) can be used to list and filter only bookmarks:

``` highlight
â¯ nb bookmark
Add: nb <url> Help: nb help bookmark
------------------------------------
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example.bookmark.md.enc
[2] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.com)
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)

â¯ nb bookmark list two
[2] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.com)
```

Bookmarks are also included in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), and [`nb list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list):

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[7] ğŸ”– Bookmark Three (example.com)
[6] Example Note
[5] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.net)
[4] Sample Note
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example-encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
[2] Demo Note
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)
```

Use the [`--type <type>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`--<type>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) option as a filter to display only bookmarks:

``` highlight
â¯ nb --type bookmark
[7] ğŸ”– Bookmark Three (example.com)
[5] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.net)
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example-encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)

â¯ nb --bookmark
[7] ğŸ”– Bookmark Three (example.com)
[5] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.net)
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example-encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} saves the domain in the title, making it easy to filter by domain using any list subcommands:

``` highlight
â¯ nb example.com
[7] ğŸ”– Bookmark Three (example.com)
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)
```

For more listing options, see [`nb help ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`nb help list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list), and [`nb help bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-aliases-nb-bk-nb-bm){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-aliases-nb-bk-nb-bm"} Shortcut Aliases: `nb bk`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `nb bm`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) can also be used with the aliases [`nb bk`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) and [`nb bm`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark):

``` highlight
â¯ nb bk
Add: nb <url> Help: nb help bookmark
------------------------------------
[7] ğŸ”– Bookmark Three (example.com)
[5] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.net)
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example-encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
[1] ğŸ”– Bookmark One (example.com)

â¯ nb bm example.net
[5] ğŸ”– Bookmark Two (example.net)
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#viewing-bookmarks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="viewing-bookmarks"} Viewing Bookmarks

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nbÂ browse`](#browse),\ [`nbÂ open`](#open),\ [`nbÂ peek`](#peek),\ [`nbÂ show`](#show)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} provides multiple ways to view bookmark files, bookmarked content, and bookmarked URLs.

Use [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) (shortcut: [`nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse)) to [browse](#-browsing) bookmarks with cached content, [\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking), linked [#tags](#-tagging), and external links:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse text:formats/markdown/123
â¯nb Â· text : formats / markdown / 123 Â· â†“ Â· edit | +
Daring Fireball: Markdown (daringfireball.net)

https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/

Related

  â€¢ https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown

Comments

See also:

  â€¢ [[text:formats/org]]
  â€¢ [[cli:apps/nb]]

Tags

#markup #plain-text

Content

Daring Fireball: Markdown

Download

Markdown 1.0.1 (18 KB)â€‰â€”â€‰17 Dec 2004

Introduction

Markdown is a text-to-HTML conversion tool for web writers. Markdown allows
you to write using an easy-to-read, easy-to-write plain text format, then
convert it to structurally valid XHTML (or HTML).
```

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

[`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) (shortcut: [`nb o`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open)) opens the bookmarked URL in your system's primary web browser:

``` highlight
# open bookmark by id
nb open 3

# open bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb open example:12

# open bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 open

# open bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:open 12
```

*N.B. To use [`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) with [WSL](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/wsl/install), install [wslu](https://github.com/wslutilities/wslu).*

[`nb peek`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek) (shortcut: [`nb p`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek), alias: [`nb preview`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek)) opens the bookmarked URL in your terminal web browser, such as [w3m](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m), [Links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)), or [Lynx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynx_(web_browser)):

``` highlight
# peek bookmark by id
nb peek 3

# peek bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb peek example:12

# peek bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 peek

# peek bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:peek 12
```

[`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) and [`nb peek`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek) work seamlessly with encrypted bookmarks. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} simply prompts you for the bookmark's password.

[`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) and [`nb peek`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek) automatically check whether the URL is still valid. If the page has been removed, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can check the [Internet Archive Wayback Machine](https://archive.org/web/) for an archived copy.

The preferred terminal web browser can be set using the `$BROWSER`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} environment variable, assigned in `~/.bashrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `~/.zshrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, or similar:

``` highlight
export BROWSER=lynx
```

When `$BROWSER`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is not set, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} looks for [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m), [`links`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)), and [`lynx`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynx_(web_browser)) and uses the first one it finds.

`$BROWSER`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can also be used to easy specify the terminal browser for an individual command:

``` highlight
â¯ BROWSER=links nb 12 peek
# opens the URL from bookmark 12 in links

â¯ BROWSER=w3m nb 12 peek
# opens the URL from bookmark 12 in w3m
```

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) and [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) can also be used to view and edit bookmark files, which include the cached page converted to Markdown.

[`nb show <id> --render`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`nb show <id> -r`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) displays the bookmark file converted to HTML in the terminal web browser, including all bookmark fields and the cached page content, providing a cleaned-up, distraction-free, locally-served view of the page content along with all of your notes.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-aliases-nb-o-and-nb-p){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-aliases-nb-o-and-nb-p"} Shortcut Aliases: `nb o`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `nb p`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) and [`nb peek`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek) can also be used with the shortcut aliases [`nb o`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) and [`nb p`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek):

``` highlight
# open bookmark by id
nb o 3

# open bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb o example:12

# open bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 o

# peek bookmark by id
nb p 3

# peek bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb p example:12

# peek bookmark 12 in the notebook named "example", alternative
nb example:12 p
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#bookmark-file-format){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="bookmark-file-format"} Bookmark File Format

Bookmarks are identified by a `.bookmark.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file extension. The bookmark URL is the first URL in the file within `<`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} characters. To create a minimally valid bookmark file with [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add):

``` highlight
nb add example.bookmark.md --content "<https://example.com>"
```

For a full overview, see [`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Markdown Bookmark File Format](#nb-markdown-bookmark-file-format).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#bookmark--a-command-line-tool-for-managing-bookmarks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="bookmark--a-command-line-tool-for-managing-bookmarks"} `bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} -- A command line tool for managing bookmarks. {#bookmark--a-command-line-tool-for-managing-bookmarks}

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes [`bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark-help), a full-featured command line interface for creating, viewing, searching, and editing bookmarks.

[`bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark-help) is a shortcut for the [`nb bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) subcommand, accepting all of the same subcommands and options with identical behavior.

Bookmark a page:

``` highlight
â¯ bookmark https://example.com --tags tag1,tag2
Added: [3] ğŸ”– 20200101000000.bookmark.md "Example Title (example.com)"
```

List and filter bookmarks with [`bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) and [`bookmark list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark):

``` highlight
â¯ bookmark
Add: bookmark <url> Help: bookmark help
---------------------------------------
[3] ğŸ”– ğŸ”’ example.bookmark.md.enc
[2] ğŸ”– Example Two (example.com)
[1] ğŸ”– Example One (example.com)

â¯ bookmark list two
[2] ğŸ”– Example Two (example.com)
```

View a bookmark in your terminal web browser:

``` highlight
bookmark peek 2
```

Open a bookmark in your system's primary web browser:

``` highlight
bookmark open 2
```

Perform a full text search of bookmarks and archived page content:

``` highlight
â¯ bookmark search "example query"
[10] ğŸ”– example.bookmark.md "Example Bookmark (example.com)"
------------------------------------------------------------
5:Lorem ipsum example query.
```
