See [`bookmark help`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark-help) for more information.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-todos){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-todos"} âœ… Todos {#-todos}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb do`](#do),\ [`nb tasks`](#tasks),\ [`nb todo`](#todo),\ [`nb undo`](#undo)^

Use [`nb todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) (shortcut: [`nb t`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo)) to create, list, and update todos. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} todos are [structured Markdown documents](#nb-markdown-todo-file-format) referencing a single primary todo, with optional [tasks](#%EF%B8%8F-tasks).

Use [`nb todo add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) to create a new todo:

``` highlight
# create a new todo titled "Example todo one."
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo one."
Added: [1] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo one.

â¯ nb show 1 --print
# [ ] Example todo one.
```

Use the [`--due <date>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) option to add an optional due date in a [`## Due`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-due) section:

``` highlight
# create a new todo titled "Example todo two." with a due date of "2100-01-01"
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo two." --due "2100-01-01"
Added: [2] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo two.

â¯ nb show 2 --print
# [ ] Example todo two.

## Due

2100-01-01
```

Add an optional [description](#-description-1) with the [`--description <description>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) option:

``` highlight
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo three." --description "Example description."
Added: [3] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo three.

â¯ nb show 3 --print
# [ ] Example todo three.

## Description

Example description.
```

Todos can have [tasks](#%EF%B8%8F-tasks). Tasks added with one or more [`--task <task>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) options are represented as a markdown task list and placed in a [`## Tasks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-tasks) section:

``` highlight
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo seven." --task "Task one." --task "Task two." --task "Task three."
Added: [7] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo seven.

â¯ nb show 7 --print
# [ ] Example todo seven.

## Tasks

- [ ] Task one.
- [ ] Task two.
- [ ] Task three.
```

Related URLs and [linked](#-linking) [selectors](#-selectors) can be added to a [`## Related`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-related-1) field using the [`-r (<url> | <selector>)`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) / [`--related (<url> | <selector>)`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) option:

``` highlight
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo four." --related example:123 -r https://example.com
Added: [4] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo four.

â¯ nb show 4 --print
# [ ] Example todo four.

## Related

- [[example:123]]
- <https://example.com>
```

[Tags](#-tagging) can be added to todos with the [`--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) option:

``` highlight
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo five." --tags tag1,tag2
Added: [5] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo five.

â¯ nb show 5 --print
# [ ] Example todo five.

## Tags

#tag1 #tag2
```

[Tags](#-tagging), [links](#-linking), and URLs can be [browsed](#-browsing) in terminal and GUI web browers with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#listing-todos){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="listing-todos"} Listing Todos

List todos in with [`nb todos`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo):

``` highlight
# list todos in the current notebook
â¯ nb todos
[6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.
[5] âœ… [x] Example todo five.
[4] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo four.
[3] âœ… [x] Example todo three.
[2] âœ… [x] Example todo two.
[1] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo one.

# list todos in the notebook named "sample"
â¯ nb todos sample:
[sample:4] âœ… [x] Sample todo four.
[sample:3] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Sample todo three.
[sample:2] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Sample todo two.
[sample:1] âœ… [x] Sample todo one.
```

Open / undone todos can be listed with [`nb todos open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo):

``` highlight
# list open todos in the current notebook
â¯ nb todos open
[6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.
[4] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo four.
[1] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo one.

# list open todos in the notebook named "sample"
â¯ nb tasks open sample:
[sample:3] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Sample todo three.
[sample:2] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Sample todo two.
```

Closed / done todos can be listed with [`nb todos closed`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo):

``` highlight
# list closed todos in the current notebook
â¯ nb todos closed
[5] âœ… [x] Example todo five.
[3] âœ… [x] Example todo three.
[2] âœ… [x] Example todo two.

# list closed todos in the notebook named "sample"
â¯ nb tasks closed sample:
[sample:4] âœ… [x] Sample todo four.
[sample:1] âœ… [x] Sample todo one.
```

See [`nb help todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) for more information.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#do--undo){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="do--undo"} `do`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} / `undo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} {#do--undo}

Mark a todo as done or closed with [`nb do`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#do):

``` highlight
# add a new todo titled "Example todo six."
â¯ nb todo add "Example todo six."
Added: [6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.

# mark todo 6 as done / closed
â¯ nb do 6
Done: [6] âœ… [x] Example todo six.
```

Re-open a closed todo with [`nb undo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#undo):

``` highlight
# mark todo 6 as undone / open
â¯ nb undo 6
Undone: [6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.
```

See [`nb help do`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#do) and [`nb help undo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#undo) for more information.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#ï¸-tasks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="ï¸-tasks"} âœ”ï¸ Tasks {#ï¸-tasks}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb do`](#do),\ [`nb tasks`](#tasks),\ [`nb todo`](#todo),\ [`nb undo`](#undo)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can list and update tasks in [todos](#-todos) and other Markdown documents.

Tasks are defined as one or more Markdown list items starting with `- [ ]`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to indicate an open task or `- [x]`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to indicate a done / closed task:

``` highlight
- [ ] Example open task.
- [x] Example closed task.
```

List tasks in items, folders, and notebooks with [`nb tasks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks) (shortcut: [`nb t`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks)), which lists both tasks and todos:

``` highlight
# list tasks in item 7
â¯ nb tasks 7
[7] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo seven.
------------------------------
[7 1] [x] Task one.
[7 2] [x] Task two.
[7 3] [ ] Task three.

# list tasks and todos in the notebook named "example"
â¯ nb tasks example:
[example:9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
[example:8] âœ… [x] Example todo eight.
--------------------------------------
[example:8 1] [x] Task one.
[example:8 2] [x] Task two.

[example:6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.
[example:4] Example Note Title
------------------------------
[example:4 1] [ ] Task one.
[example:4 2] [x] Task two.
[example:4 3] [ ] Task three.

[example:3] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo three.
```

Open / undone tasks can be listed with [`nb tasks open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks):

``` highlight
# list open tasks in item 7
â¯ nb tasks open 7
[7] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo seven.
------------------------------
[7 3] [ ] Task three.

# list open tasks and todos in the notebook named "example"
â¯ nb tasks open example:
[example:9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
[example:6] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo six.
[example:4] Example Note Title
------------------------------
[example:4 1] [ ] Task one.
[example:4 3] [ ] Task three.

[example:3] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo three.
```

Closed / done tasks can be listed with [`nb tasks closed`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks):

``` highlight
# list closed tasks in item 7
â¯ nb tasks closed 7
[7] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo seven.
------------------------------
[7 1] [x] Task one.
[7 2] [x] Task two.

# list closed tasks and todos in the notebook named "example"
â¯ nb tasks closed example:
[example:8] âœ… [x] Example todo eight.
--------------------------------------
[example:8 1] [x] Task one.
[example:8 2] [x] Task two.

[example:4] Example Note Title
------------------------------
[example:4 2] [x] Task two.
```

Tasks are identified by the item [selector](#-selectors), followed by a space, then followed by the sequential number of the task in the file.

Use [`nb do`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#do) to mark tasks as done / closed:

``` highlight
# list tasks in item 9
â¯ nb tasks 9
[9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
-----------------------------
[9 1] [ ] Task one.
[9 2] [ ] Task two.
[9 3] [ ] Task three.

# mark task 2 in item 9 as done / closed
â¯ nb do 9 2
[9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
-----------------------------
Done: [9 2] [x] Task two.

# list tasks in item 9
â¯ nb tasks 9
[9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
-----------------------------
[9 1] [ ] Task one.
[9 2] [x] Task two.
[9 3] [ ] Task three.
```

Undo a done / closed task with [`nb undo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#undo):

``` highlight
# mark task 2 in item 9 as undone / open
â¯ nb undo 9 2
[9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
-----------------------------
Undone: [9 2] [ ] Task two.

# list tasks in item 9
â¯ nb tasks 9
[9] âœ”ï¸ [ ] Example todo nine.
-----------------------------
[9 1] [ ] Task one.
[9 2] [ ] Task two.
[9 3] [ ] Task three.
```

See [`nb help tasks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks) for more information.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-tagging){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-tagging"} ğŸ· #tagging {#-tagging}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb add`](#add),\ [`nb bookmark`](#bookmark),\ [`nb browse`](#browse),\ [`nb list`](#list),\ [`nb ls`](#ls),\ [`nb search`](#search)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} recognizes `#hashtags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} defined anywhere within a document. A hashtag is defined in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} as a `#`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} character followed by any number of letters, numbers, underscores, and dashes.

Notes and bookmarks can be tagged when they are created using the `--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} option, which is available with [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`nb <url>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help), [`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), [`nb bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark), and [`nb todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo). `--tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} takes a comma-separated list of tags, converts them to `#hashtags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, and adds them to the document.

Tags added to notes with [`nb add --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) are placed between the title and body text:

``` highlight
â¯ nb add --title "Example Title" "Example note content." --tags tag1,tag2
```

``` highlight
# Example Title

#tag1 #tag2

Example note content.
```

Tags added to [bookmarks](#bookmarks) with [`nb <url> --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help) and [`nb bookmark <url> --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark) are placed in a [`## Tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-tags) section:

``` highlight
â¯ nb https://example.com --tags tag1,tag2
```

``` highlight
# Example Title (example.com)

<https://example.com>

## Description

Example description.

## Tags

#tag1 #tag2

## Content

Example Title
=============

This domain is for use in illustrative examples in documents. You may
use this domain in literature without prior coordination or asking for
permission.

[More information\...](https://www.iana.org/domains/example)
```

Tags added to [todos](#-todos) with [`nb todo add --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo) are placed in a [`## Tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-tags-1) section:

``` highlight
â¯ nb todo add --tags tag1,tag2 "Example todo."
```

``` highlight
# [ ] Example todo.

## Tags

#tag1 #tag2
```

Use [`nb --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help), [`nb ls --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), and [`nb list --tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list) to list the tags present in a notebook, folder, or item:

``` highlight
# list all tags found in items in the current notebook
nb --tags

# list all tags found in the folder named "example"
nb example/ --tags

# list all tags in the item with id 123 in the notebook named "sample"
nb sample:123 --tags
```

List tagged items by passing `\#escaped`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or `"#quoted"`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} hashtags or tags specified with the [`--tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) option to [`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls):

``` highlight
# list items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1", escaped
nb \#tag1

# list items in the "example" notebook tagged with "#tag2", quoted
nb example: "#tag2"

# list items in all notebooks tagged with "#tag3", long option
nb --tags tag3 --all

# list items in all notebooks tagged with "#tag3", short option
nb --tags tag3 -a
```

Combine multiple tags to search for items containing all specified tags:

``` highlight
# list items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb \#tag1 "#tag2"

# list items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag2" AND "#tag3"
nb --tags tag2,tag3

# list items in all notebooks tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2" AND "#tag3" AND "#tag4"
nb \#tag1 "#tag2" --tags tag3,tag4 --all
```

Tagged items can be [searched](#-search) with [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search):

``` highlight
# search for items tagged with "#tag1"
nb search --tag tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut and short option
nb q -t tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut and argument
nb q \#tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut and argument, alternative
nb q "#tag1"

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb q --tag tag1 --tag tag2

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2", short options
nb q -t tag1 -t tag2

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2", arguments
nb q \#tag1 \#tag2

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2", tag list
nb q --tags tag1,tag2

# search for items tagged with either "#tag1" OR "#tag2", options
nb q -t tag1 --or -t tag2

# search for items tagged with either "#tag1" OR "#tag2", arguments
nb q \#tag1 --or \#tag2

# search for items tagged with either "#tag1" OR "#tag2", single argument
nb q "#tag1|#tag2"

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2" AND "#tag3"
nb q -t tag1 --tags tag2,tag3

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2" OR "#tag3"
nb q -t tag1 --or --tags tag2,tag3

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2" OR "#tag3"
nb q \#tag1 --or -t tag2 --or "#tag3"
```

Linked tags can be [browsed](#-browsing) with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), providing another dimension of browsability in terminal and GUI web browsers, complimenting [\[\[wiki-style linking\]\]](#-linking).

Tags in notes, bookmarks, files in text-based formats, Word `.docx`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} documents, and [Open Document](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenDocument) `.odt`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files are rendered as links to the list of items in the notebook sharing that tag:

``` highlight
â¯nb Â· example : 321

Example Title

#tag1 #tag2

Example content with link to [[Sample Title]].

More example content:

- one
- two
- three
```

Use the [`-t <tag>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`--tag <tag>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) option to open [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) to the list of all items in the current notebook or a specified notebook or folder that share a tag:

``` highlight
# open to a list of items tagged with "#tag2" in the "example" notebook
â¯ nb browse example: --tag tag2
â¯nb Â· example

search: [#tag2               ]

[example:321]Â Example Title
[example:654]Â Sample Title
[example:789]Â Demo Title

# shortcut alias and short option
â¯ nb b example: -t tag2
â¯nb Â· example

search: [#tag2               ]

[example:321]Â Example Title
[example:654]Â Sample Title
[example:789]Â Demo Title
```

For more information about full-text search, see [Search](#-search) and [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search). For more information about browsing, see [Browsing](#-browsing) and [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-linking){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-linking"} ğŸ”— Linking {#-linking}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb browse`](#browse)^

Notes, bookmarks, files in text-based formats, Word `.docx`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} documents, and [Open Document](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenDocument) `.odt`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files can reference other items using [\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking), making `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} a powerful terminal-first platform for [Zettelkasten](#-zettelkasten), wiki-style knowledge mapping, and other link-based note-taking methods.

To add a link from a note or bookmark to another in the same notebook, include the id, title, or relative path for the target item within double square brackets anywhere in the linking document:

``` highlight
# link to the item with id 123 in the root level of current notebook
[[123]]

# link to the item titled "Example Title" in the root level of the current notebook
[[Example Title]]

# link to the item with id 456 in the folder named "Sample Folder"
[[Sample Folder/456]]

# link to the item titled "Demo Title" in the folder named "Sample Folder"
[[Sample Folder/Demo Title]]
```

To link to an item in another notebook, add the notebook name with a colon before the identifier:

``` highlight
# link to the item with id 123 in the "sample" folder in the "example" notebook
[[example:sample/123]]

# link to the item titled "Example Title" in the "demo" notebook
[[demo:Example Title]]

# link to the item with filename "Example File.md" in the "sample" notebook
[[sample:Example File.md]]
```

The text for a link can be specified after a pipe `|`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} character:

``` highlight
# render link to item 123 in the "example" notebook as [[Example Link Text]]
[[example:123|Example Link Text]]
```

[\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking) cooperate well with [Org links](https://orgmode.org/guide/Hyperlinks.html), which have a similar syntax, providing a convenient option for linking collections of Org files.

Linked items can be [browsed](#-browsing) with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

For more information about identifying items, see [Selectors](#-selectors).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-browsing){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-browsing"} ğŸŒ Browsing {#-browsing}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb browse`](#browse)^

Use [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) (shortcut: [`nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse)) to browse, view, edit, and search linked notes, bookmarks, notebooks, folders, and other items using terminal and GUI web browsers.

![nb browse](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/gui-gui-terminal-browse.png){width="500"}

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) includes an embedded, terminal-first web application that renders [\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking) and [#hashtags](#-tagging) as internal links, enabling you to browse your notes and notebooks in web browsers, including seamlessly browsing to and from the offsite links in bookmarks and notes.

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse
â¯nb Â· home : +

search: [                    ]

[home:6]Â  ğŸ“Œ ExampleÂ MarkdownÂ Title
[home:12]Â ğŸ”’Â example-encrypted.md.enc
[home:11]Â ğŸ”–Â ExampleÂ BookmarkÂ (example.com)
[home:10]Â ğŸ”–Â ğŸ”’Â example-encrypted.bookmark.md.enc
[home:9]Â Â ExampleÂ .orgÂ Title
[home:8]Â Â ğŸŒ„Â example-image.png
[home:7]Â Â ğŸ“„Â example.pdf
[home:5]Â Â ğŸ”‰Â example-audio.mp3
[home:4]Â Â ExampleÂ LaTeXÂ Title
[home:3]Â Â ğŸ“¹Â example-video.mp4
[home:2]Â Â example.md
[home:1]Â Â ğŸ“‚Â ExampleÂ Folder
```

Lists are displayed using the same format as `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), including [pinned](#-pinning) items, with each list item linked. Lists are automatically paginated to fit the height of the terminal window.

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse example:sample/demo/
â¯nb Â· example : sample / demo / +

search: [                    ]

[example:sample/demo/7] Title Seven
[example:sample/demo/6] Title Six
[example:sample/demo/5] Title Five
[example:sample/demo/4] Title Four
[example:sample/demo/3] Title Three

next â¯
```

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) is designed to make it easy to navigate within terminal web browsers using only keyboard commands, while also supporting mouse interactions. The [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) interface includes links to quickly jump to parent folders, the current notebook, and other notebooks.

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) opens in [w3m](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m), [Links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_\(web_browser\)), or in the browser set in the `$BROWSER`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} environment variable. Use [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b -g`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) to open in the system's primary [GUI web browser](#browse---gui).

To open a specific item in [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), pass the [selector](#-selectors) for the item, folder, or notebook to [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
# open the item with id 42 in the folder named "sample" in the "example" notebook
â¯ nb browse example:sample/42
â¯nb Â· example : sample / 42 Â· â†“ Â· edit | +

Example Title

#tag1 #tag2

Example content with link to [[Demo Title]].

More example content:

  â€¢ one
  â€¢ two
  â€¢ three
```

Items can also be browsed with [`nb show --browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) / [`nb s -b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show), which behaves identically.

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) is particularly useful for [bookmarks](#-bookmarks). Cached content is rendered in the web browser along with comments and notes. Internal and external links are easily accessible directly in the terminal, providing a convenient, distraction-free approach for browsing collections of bookmarks.

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse text:formats/markdown/123
â¯nb Â· text : formats / markdown / 123 Â· â†“ Â· edit | +
Daring Fireball: Markdown (daringfireball.net)

https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/

Related

  â€¢ https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown

Comments

See also:

  â€¢ [[text:formats/org]]
  â€¢ [[cli:apps/nb]]

Tags

#markup #plain-text

Content

Daring Fireball: Markdown

Download

Markdown 1.0.1 (18 KB)â€‰â€”â€‰17 Dec 2004

Introduction

Markdown is a text-to-HTML conversion tool for web writers. Markdown allows
you to write using an easy-to-read, easy-to-write plain text format, then
convert it to structurally valid XHTML (or HTML).
```

Notes, bookmarks, files in text-based formats, source code, Word `.docx`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} documents, and [Open Document](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenDocument) `.odt`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files are converted into HTML and rendered in the browser. Use the down arrow (`â†“`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}) link to view or download the original file.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-edit){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-edit"} `browse edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

![nb browse edit](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/gui-terminal-browse-edit.png){width="500"}

Items in text formats can be edited within terminal and GUI web browsers using the `edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} link on the item page or by opening the item with [`nb browse edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b e`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), which automatically resizes the form to fit the current terminal window:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse edit text:formats/markdown/123
â¯nb Â· text : formats / markdown / 123 Â· â†“ Â· editing Â· - | +

[# Daring Fireball: Markdown (daringfireball.net)         ]
[                                                         ]
[<https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/>          ]
[                                                         ]
[## Related                                               ]
[                                                         ]
[- <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markdown>               ]
[                                                         ]
[## Comments                                              ]
[                                                         ]
[See also:                                                ]
[                                                         ]
[- [[text:formats/org]]                                   ]
[- [[cli:apps/nb]]                                        ]
[                                                         ]
[## Tags                                                  ]
[                                                         ]

[save] Â·Â last: 2021-01-01 01:00:00
```

Terminal web browsers provide different editing workflows. [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m) opens items in your `$EDITOR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, then returns you back to the browser to save changes and continue browsing. Edits in [`links`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)) are performed directly in the browser.

Syntax highlighting, block selection, and other [advanced editor features](#browse---gui-editing) are available with [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-add){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-add"} `browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Add an item within the browser using the `+`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} link or [`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b a`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse). Pass a notebook, folder, and / or filename selector to create a new note in that location:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse add text:formats/
â¯nb Â· text : formats / +

[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]

[add]
```

[`nb browse add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) includes options for quickly pre-populating new notes with content:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse add --title "Example Title" --content "Example content." --tags tag1,tag2
â¯nb Â· home : +

[# Example Title                                    ]
[                                                   ]
[#tag1 #tag2                                        ]
[                                                   ]
[Example content.                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]
[                                                   ]

[add]
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-delete){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-delete"} `browse delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Use the `-`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} link on the [`nb browse edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) page or [`nb browse delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b d`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) to delete an item:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse delete example:4
â¯nb Â· example : 4 Â· â†“ Â· edit Â· - | +

              deleting

[4] example_file.md "Example Title"

              [delete]
Â 
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-search){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-search"} `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Search

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) includes a search field powered by [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) that can be used to search the current notebook or folder. Search queries are treated as command line arguments for [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search), providing the ability to perform `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `OR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries. Use the [`-q <query>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`--query <query>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) option to open [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) to the results page for a search:

``` highlight
# open to a list of items containing "example" in the current notebook
â¯ nb browse --query "example"
â¯nb Â· home

search: [example             ]

[home:321]Â Test Title
[home:654]Â Sample Title
[home:789]Â Demo Title

# using shortcut alias and short option
â¯ nb b -q "example"
â¯nb Â· home

search: [example             ]

[home:321]Â Test Title
[home:654]Â Sample Title
[home:789]Â Demo Title
```

Search for [#tags](#-tagging) with the [`-t`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`--tag`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`--tags`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) options:

``` highlight
# open to a list of items tagged with "#tag2" in the current notebook
â¯ nb browse --tag tag2
â¯nb Â· home

search: [#tag2               ]

[home:654]Â Sample Title
[home:789]Â Demo Title

# using shortcut alias and short option
â¯ nb b -t tag2
â¯nb Â· home

search: [#tag2               ]

[home:654]Â Sample Title
[home:789]Â Demo Title
```

For more information about search options, see [Search](#-search) and [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse---gui){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse---gui"} `browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

To open any [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) view in the system's primary GUI web browser, add the [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b -g`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) option:

``` highlight
# open the item with id 123 in the "sample" notebook in the system's primary GUI browser
nb browse sample:123 --gui

# open the folder named "example" in the system's primary GUI browser,
# short option
nb browse example/ -g

# open the current notebook in the system's primary GUI browser,
# shortcut alias and short option
nb b -g
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse---gui-editing){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse---gui-editing"} `browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Editing

By default, [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) uses the browser's default `<textarea>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} for editing items.

[Ace](https://ace.c9.io/) is a text editor for GUI web browsers that provides advanced text editing functionality, including block selection and [syntax highlighting](#gui-web-syntax-highlighting).

To use Ace as the editor for [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), add the following line to your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file:

``` highlight
export NB_ACE_ENABLED=1
```

The next time a form is loaded in [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} will automatically download (from [GitHub](https://github.com/ajaxorg/ace-builds/)), install, and enable the Ace editor in [`nb browse edit --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) and [`nb browse add --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-portability){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-portability"} `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Portability

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) depends on [`ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://nmap.org/ncat/), which is available as part of the `ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or `nmap`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} package in most package managers, and [`pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://pandoc.org/). When only `pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is available, the current note is rendered and [\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking) go to unrendered, original files. If only `ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is available, files in plain text formats are rendered with the original markup unconverted. If neither `ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} nor `pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is available, [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) falls back to the default behavior of [`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-privacy){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-privacy"} `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Privacy

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) is completely local and self-contained within `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, from the CSS and JavaScript all the way down through the HTTP request parsing and response building, with no imports, libraries, frameworks, or third-party code outside of the few binary dependencies (`bash`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `ncat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}), the Linux / Unix environment, and the optional [Ace editor](#ace-editor).

Terminal web browsers don't use JavaScript, so visits from them are not visible to some web analytics tools. [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) includes a number of additional features to enhance privacy and avoid leaking information:

-   Page content is cached locally within each bookmark file, making it readable in terminal and GUI web browsers without requesting the page again or needing to be connected to the internet.
-   `<img>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} tags in bookmarked content are removed to avoid requests.
-   Outbound links are automatically rewritten to use an [exit page redirect](https://geekthis.net/post/hide-http-referer-headers/#exit-page-redirect) to mitigate leaking information via the [referer header](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Headers/Referer).
-   All pages include the `<meta name="referrer" content="no-referrer" />`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} tag.
-   Links include a `rel="noopener noreferrer"`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} attribute.
-   `lynx`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is opened with the `-noreferer`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} option.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse-asciidoc){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse-asciidoc"} `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} AsciiDoc

To [`browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) items in [AsciiDoc](https://asciidoc.org/) format, install [`asciidoctor`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://asciidoctor.org/).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-alias-nb-b){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-alias-nb-b"} Shortcut Alias: `nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) can also be used with the alias [`nb b`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
# open the current notebook in the terminal web browser
nb b

# open the item with id 123 in the "example" notebook using the terminal web browser
nb b example:123

# open the notebook named "sample" in the GUI web browser
nb b sample: -g
```

For more information, see [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-images){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-images"} ğŸŒ„ Images {#-images}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb browse`](#browse),\ [`nb import`](#import),\ [`nb open`](#open),\ [`nb show`](#show)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can be used to view, organize, browse, reference, and work with images in terminals, web browsers, and GUI applications.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#image-items){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="image-items"} Image Items

[Import](#%EF%B8%8F-import--export) images with [`nb import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import):

``` highlight
# import the image file "example.png" into the current notebook
nb import example.png

# import an image file from a URL into the current notebook
nb import https://raw.githubusercontent.com/xwmx/nb/master/docs/images/nb.png

# nb import "sample.jpg" into the "demo" folder in the "example" notebook
nb import sample.jpg example:demo/
```

Imported images are displayed with [`ğŸŒ„`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} indicators](#indicators) in [lists](#listing--filtering):

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[5] Example Five
[4] ğŸŒ„ example-image.png
[3] Example Three
[2] Example Two
[1] Example One
```

Imported image items can be opened in the system GUI application for the item's file type using [`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open):

``` highlight
# open the image "example-image.png" in the system GUI photo viewer
nb open example-image.png

# open the image with id "4" in the system GUI photo viewer
nb 4 o
```

Image items can be viewed in web browsers with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), providing a convenient mechanism for [browsing](#-browsing) notebooks and folders containing image collections.

[`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) renders image items within in an `<img>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} tag on the item page. Open the item page for an image item by passing a [selector](#-selectors) to [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), optionally including the [`-g`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`--gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) option to open the page in the system GUI web browser:

``` highlight
# open item with id "123" in the terminal web browser
nb browse 123

# open item with id "456" in the "example" notebook in the GUI web browser
nb browse example:456 --gui

# open item "example:456" in the GUI web browser, alternative
nb example:456 b -g
```

The original file can be viewed or downloaded from the item page by either clicking the image item or using the down arrow (`â†“`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}) link.

[`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse---gui) displays images in any GUI web browser. Some terminal web browsers, such as [`w3m`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](http://w3m.sourceforge.net/), can be configured to display images.

[`nb show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) can display images directly in the terminal with supported tools and configurations, including:

-   [`catimg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/posva/catimg)
-   [Chafa](https://github.com/hpjansson/chafa)
-   [ImageMagick](https://imagemagick.org/) with a terminal that supports [sixels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sixel)
-   [`imgcat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://www.iterm2.com/documentation-images.html) with [iTerm2](https://www.iterm2.com/)
-   [kitty's `icat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} kitten](https://sw.kovidgoyal.net/kitty/kittens/icat.html)
-   [`term-image`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/AnonymouX47/term-image)
-   [`timg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/hzeller/timg)
-   [`viu`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/atanunq/viu)

A preferred image viewer tool can be set with the [`$NB_IMAGE_TOOL`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_image_tool) variable in your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file, which can be opened in your editor with [`nb settings edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#inline-images){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="inline-images"} Inline Images

Images can be referenced and rendered inline within notes, bookmarks, and other items.

To reference an image in the same notebook, specify the image's relative path within the notebook:

``` highlight
# reference "example.jpg" from markdown
![](example.jpg)

# reference "demo.png" in the "sample" folder from markdown
![](sample/demo.png)
```

Images in any notebook can be referenced using the `--original`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} URL, obtainable from the image's [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) item page by either clicking the image item or using the down arrow (`â†“`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}) link.

``` highlight
# reference "example.jpg" in the "home" notebook with the --original URL
![](http://localhost:6789/--original/home/example.jpg)
```

Image references in content are rendered inline within web browsers with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) and [`nb show --render`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show).

`<img>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} tags are stripped from bookmarked content when rendering to HTML. Inline images can still be used in other bookmark sections like [`## Comment`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-comment).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-zettelkasten){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-zettelkasten"} ğŸ—‚ Zettelkasten {#-zettelkasten}

^[â†‘](#overview)^

Zettelkasten (German: "slip box") is a method of note-taking and personal knowledge management modeled around a few key features:

-   Notes are taken liberally on index cards.
-   Each note is numbered for easy reference.
-   Index cards are organized into boxes.
-   Index cards can reference other index cards.
-   Cards can include tags and other metadata.

Since `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} works directly on plain text files organized in normal system directories in normal git repositories, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is a very close digital analogue to physical zettelkasten note-taking.

     Zettelkasten                                             `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}
  ------------------ -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     index cards                                               [notes](#-notes) & [bookmarks](#-bookmarks)
      numbering                                                      ids & [selectors](#-selectors)
      slip boxes                                                        [notebooks](#-notebooks)
         tags                                                              [#tags](#-tagging)
       metadata                                                       [front matter](#front-matter)
   cross-references                                               [\[\[wiki-style links\]\]](#-linking)
   fast note-taking   [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#adding)/[`nb <url>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#-bookmarks)

For more information about Zettelkasten, see [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zettelkasten).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-folders){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-folders"} ğŸ“‚ Folders {#-folders}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb add`](#add),\ [`nb browse`](#browse),\ [`nb folders`](#folders),\ [`nb list`](#list),\ [`nb ls`](#ls)^

Items can be organized in folders. To add a note to a folder, call [`nb add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add) with the folder's relative path within the notebook followed by a slash:

``` highlight
# add a new note in the folder named "example"
nb add example/

# add a new note in the folder named "demo" in "example"
nb add example/demo/
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} automatically creates any intermediate folders as needed.

Folders can be created directly using [`nb add folder`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`nb folders add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#folders), and [`nb add --type folder`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add):

``` highlight
# create a new folder named "sample"
nb add folder sample

# create a new folder named "sample", alternative
nb folders add sample

# create a new folder named "demo"
nb add demo --type folder

# create a folder named "example" containing a folder named "test"
nb add example/test --type folder
```

To list the items in a folder, pass the folder relative path to `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`nb list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list), or [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) with a trailing slash:

``` highlight
â¯ nb example/demo/
home
----
[example/demo/3] Title Three
[example/demo/2] Title Two
[example/demo/1] Title One
```

Folders can also be identified by the folder's id and listed with a trailing slash:

``` highlight
â¯ nb list
[1] ğŸ“‚ example

â¯ nb list 1/
[example/2] ğŸ“‚ demo
[example/1] document.md

â¯ nb list 1/2/
[example/demo/3] Title Three
[example/demo/2] Title Two
[example/demo/1] Title One
```

Items in folders can be idenitified with the folder's relative path using either folder ids or names, followed by the id, title, or filename of the item:

``` highlight
# list item 1 ("Title One", one.md) in the example/demo/ folder
nb list example/demo/1

# edit item 1 ("Title One", one.md) in the example/demo/ folder
nb edit example/2/one.md

# show item 1 ("Title One", one.md) in the example/demo/ folder
nb show 1/2/Title\ One

# delete item 1 ("Title One", one.md) in the example/demo/ folder
nb delete 1/demo/1
```

For folders and items in other notebooks, combine the relative path with the notebook name, separated by a colon:

``` highlight
# list the contents of the "sample" folder in the "example" notebook
nb example:sample/

# add an item to the "sample/demo" folder in the "example" notebook
nb add example:sample/demo/

# edit item 3 in the "sample/demo" folder in the "example" notebook
nb edit example:sample/demo/3
```

[Browse](#-browsing) starting at any folder with [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse example:sample/demo/
â¯nb Â· example : sample / demo /

search: [                    ]

[example:sample/demo/5] Title Five
[example:sample/demo/4] Title Four
[example:sample/demo/3] Title Three
[example:sample/demo/2] Title Two
[example:sample/demo/1] Title One
```

For more information about identifying folders, see [Selectors](#-selectors).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-pinning){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-pinning"} ğŸ“Œ Pinning {#-pinning}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb pin`](#pin),\ [`nb unpin`](#unpin),\ [`nb ls`](#ls),\ [`nb browse`](#browse)^

Items can be pinned so they appear first in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), and [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[2] ğŸ“Œ Title Two
[5] Title Five
[4] Title Four
[3] Title Three
[1] Title One
```

Use [`nb pin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#pin) and [`nb unpin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#unpin) to pin and unpin items:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[5] Title Five
[4] Title Four
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
[1] Title One

â¯ nb pin 4
Pinned: [4] four.md "Title Four"

â¯ nb pin 1
Pinned: [1] one.md "Title One"

â¯ nb
home
----
[4] ğŸ“Œ Title Four
[1] ğŸ“Œ Title One
[5] Title Five
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two

â¯ nb unpin 4
Unpinned: [4] four.md "Title Four"

â¯ nb
home
----
[1] ğŸ“Œ Title One
[5] Title Five
[4] Title Four
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can also be configured to pin notes that contain a specified [#hashtag](#-tagging) or other search pattern. To enable tag / search-based pinning, set the [`$NB_PINNED_PATTERN`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_pinned_pattern) environment variable to the desired [#tag](#-tagging) or pattern.

For example, to treat all items tagged with `#pinned`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} as pinned items, add the following line to your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file, which can be opened in your editor with [`nb settings edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings):

``` highlight
export NB_PINNED_PATTERN="#pinned"
```

All [indicator icons](#indicators) in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can be customized, so to use a different character as the pindicator, simply add a line like the following to your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file:

``` highlight
export NB_INDICATOR_PINNED="ğŸ’–"
```

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[1] ğŸ’– Title One
[5] Title Five
[4] Title Four
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
```

To bump an item to the top of the list without pinning, use the [`bump`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} plugin](#bump).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-search){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-search"} ğŸ” Search {#-search}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb search`](#search)^

Use [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) (shortcut: [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search)) to perform full text searches, with support for regular expressions, [#tags](#-tagging), and `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `OR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, and `NOT`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries:

``` highlight
# search current notebook for "example query"
nb search "example query"

# search the notebook "example" for "example query"
nb search example: "example query"

# search the folder named "demo" for "example query"
nb search demo/ "example query"

# search all unarchived notebooks for "example query" and list matching items
nb search "example query" --all --list

# search for "example" AND "demo" with multiple arguments
nb search "example" "demo"

# search for "example" AND "demo" with option
nb search "example" --and "demo"

# search for "example" OR "sample" with argument
nb search "example|sample"

# search for "example" OR "sample" with option
nb search "example" --or "sample"

# search for items matching both "Example" AND "Sample", and NOT "Demo"
nb search "Example" --and "Sample" --not "Demo"

# search items containing the hashtag "#example"
nb search "#example"

# search with a regular expression
nb search "\d\d\d-\d\d\d\d"

# search bookmarks for "example"
nb search "example" --type bookmark

# search bookmarks for "example", alternative
nb bk q "example"

# search the current notebook for "example query"
nb q "example query"

# search the notebook named "example" for "example query"
nb q example: "example query"

# search all unarchived notebooks for "example query" and list matching items
nb q -la "example query"
```

[`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) prints the id number, filename, and title of each matched file, followed by each search query match and its line number, with color highlighting:

``` highlight
â¯ nb search "example"
[314]  ğŸ”– example.bookmark.md "Example Bookmark (example.com)"
--------------------------------------------------------------
1:# Example Bookmark (example.com)

3:<https://example.com>

[2718] example.md "Example Note"
--------------------------------
1:# Example Note
```

To just print the note information line without the content matches, use the [`-l`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) or [`--list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) option:

``` highlight
â¯ nb search "example" --list
[314]  ğŸ”– example.bookmark.md "Example Bookmark (example.com)"
[2718] example.md "Example Note"
```

Multiple query arguments are treated as `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries, returning items that match all queries. `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries can also be specified with the [`--and <query>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) option:

``` highlight
# search for items tagged with "#example" AND "#demo" AND "#sample" using
# multiple arguments
nb q "#example" "#demo" "#sample"

# options
nb q "#example" --and "#demo" --and "#sample"
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} matches `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} query terms regardless of where they appear in a document, an improvement over most approaches for performing `AND`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries with command line tools, which typically only match terms appearing on the same line.

`OR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries return items that match at least one of the queries and can be created by separating terms in a single argument with a pipe character `|`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or with the [`--or <query>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) option:

``` highlight
# search for "example" OR "sample" with argument
nb q "example|sample"

# search for "example" OR "sample" with option
nb q "example" --or "sample"
```

[`--or`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) and [`--and`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) queries can be used together:

``` highlight
nb q "example" --or "sample" --and "demo"
# equivalent: example|sample AND demo|sample
```

`NOT`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} queries exclude items that match the specified query and are specified with [`--not <query>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search), which can be used with `--and`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `--or`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
# search for items that match "Example", excluding items that also match "Sample"
nb search "Example" --not "Sample"

# search for items matching both "Example" AND "Sample", and NOT "Demo"
nb search "Example" --and "Sample" --not "Demo"
```

Search for [#tags](#-tagging) with flexible [`nb search --tags [<tags>]`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q -t [<tags>]`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) options:

``` highlight
# search for tags in the current notebook
nb search --tags

# search for tags in the "sample" notebook, shortcut alias
nb sample:q --tags

# search for items tagged with "#tag1"
nb search --tag tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut alias and short option
nb q -t tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut alias and argument
nb q \#tag1

# search for items tagged with "#tag1", shortcut alias and argument, alternative
nb q "#tag1"

# search for items in the "sample" notebook tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb sample:search --tag tag1 --tag tag2

# search for items in the "sample" notebook tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb sample:q --tags tag1,tag2

# search for items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2"
nb q --tag tag1 --tag tag2

# search for items in the current notebook tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2"
nb q -t tag1 --or -t tag2

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" AND "#tag2" AND "#tag3"
nb q -t tag1 --tags tag2,tag3

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2" OR "#tag3"
nb q -t tag1 --or --tags tag2,tag3

# search for items tagged with "#tag1" OR "#tag2" OR "#tag3"
nb q \#tag1 --or -t tag2 --or "#tag3"
```

[`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) leverages Git's powerful built-in [`git grep`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-grep). `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also supports performing searches with alternative search tools using the [`--utility <name>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) option.

Supported alternative search tools:

-   [`rga`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/phiresky/ripgrep-all)
-   [`rg`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/BurntSushi/ripgrep)
-   [`ag`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/ggreer/the_silver_searcher)
-   [`ack`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://beyondgrep.com/)
-   [`grep`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grep)

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-alias-nb-q){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-alias-nb-q"} Shortcut Alias: `nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) can also be used with the alias [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) (for "query"):

``` highlight
# search for "example" and print matching excerpts
nb q "example"

# search for "example" and list each matching file
nb q -l "example"

# search for "example" in all unarchived notebooks
nb q -a "example"

# search for "example" in the notbook named "sample"
nb sample:q "example"
```

For more information about search, see [`nb help search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search).

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#searching-with-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="searching-with-browse"} Searching with `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Searches can be performed within terminal and GUI web browsers using [`nb browse --query`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) / [`nb b -q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse):

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse --query "#example"
â¯nb Â· home : +

search: [#example             ]

[home:7]   Title Seven
[home:32]  Title Thirty-Two
[home:56]  Title Fifty-Six
[home:135] Title One Hundred and Thirty-Five
```

For more information, see [Browsing](#-browsing).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-moving--renaming){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-moving--renaming"} â†” Moving & Renaming {#-moving--renaming}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb move`](#move),\ [`nb copy`](#copy)^

Use [`nb move`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) (alias: [`nb rename`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move), shortcut: [`nb mv`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move)) to move and rename items:

``` highlight
# move "example.md" to "sample.org"
nb move example.md sample.org

# rename note 2 ("example.md") to "New Name.md"
nb rename 2 "New Name"
```

Items can be moved between notebooks and folders:

``` highlight
# move note 12 from the "example" notebook into "Sample Folder" in the "demo" notebook
nb move example:12 demo:Sample\ Folder/
```

When the file extension is omitted, the existing extension is used:

``` highlight
# rename "example.bookmark.md" to "New Name.bookmark.md"
nb move example.bookmark.md "New Name"
```

When only a file extension is specified, only the extension is updated:

``` highlight
# change the file extension of note 5 ("demo file.md") to .org ("demo file.org")
nb rename 5 .org
```

Use [`nb rename --to-bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) to change the extension of a note to `.bookmark.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, [`nb rename --to-todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) to change the extension to `.todo.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, and [`nb rename --to-note`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) to change the extension of a bookmark or todo to either `.md`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or the extension set with [`nb set default_extension`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#default_extension):

``` highlight
# rename note 3 ("example.md") to a bookmark named "example.bookmark.md"
nb rename 3 --to-bookmark

# rename bookmark 6 ("sample.bookmark.md") to a note named "sample.md"
nb rename 6 --to-note

# rename note 7 ("demo.md") to a todo named "demo.todo.md"
nb rename 7 --to-todo
```

Use [`nb rename --to-title`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) to set the filename to the note title, lowercased with spaces and disallowed filename characters replaced with underscores:

``` highlight
â¯ nb rename 12 --to-title
Moving:   [12] 20210101010000.md "Example Title"
To:       example_title.md
Proceed?  [y/N]
```

Copy an item to a destination notebook, folder path, or filename with [`nb copy`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#copy) (alias: [`nb duplicate`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#copy)):

``` highlight
# copy item 456 to "sample.md"
nb copy 456 sample.md

# copy item 678 to the "example" notebook
nb copy 678 example:

# copy item 789 to the "demo" folder
nb copy 789 demo/

# copy item 543 to test.md in the "sample" folder in the "example" notebook
nb copy 543 example:sample/test.md
```

Omit a destination to copy the item in place:

``` highlight
# copy item 123 ("example.md") to example-1.md
â¯ nb copy 123
Added: [124] example-1.md

# copy item 123 ("example.md") to example-2.md, alias
â¯ nb duplicate 123
Added: [125] example-2.md
```

For more information about moving, renaming, and copying items, see [`nb help move`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move) and [`nb help copy`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#copy).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-revision-history){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-revision-history"} ğŸ—’ Revision History {#-revision-history}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb history`](#history),\ [`nb notebooks`](#notebooks)^

Whenever a note is added, modified, or deleted, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} automatically commits the change to git transparently in the background.

Use [`nb history`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#history) to view the revision history of any notebook, folder, or item:

``` highlight
# show history for current notebook
nb history

# show history for note number 4
nb history 4

# show history for note with filename example.md
nb history example.md

# show history for note titled "Example"
nb history Example

# show history for the notebook named "example"
nb example:history

# show history for the notebook named "example", alternative
nb history example:

# show the history for note 12 in the notebook named "example"
nb history example:12
```

[`nb history`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#history) uses `git log`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} by default and prefers [`tig`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/jonas/tig) when available.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#authorship){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="authorship"} Authorship

By default, git commits are attributed to the email and name configured in your [global `git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} configuration](https://git-scm.com/book/en/v2/Customizing-Git-Git-Configuration).

Change the email and name used for a notebook with [`nb notebooks author`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks):

``` highlight
# edit the commit author email and name for the current notebook
â¯ nb notebooks author
Current configuration for: home
--------------------------
email (global): example@example.test
name  (global): Example Name

Update?  [y/N]

# edit the commit author email and name for the notebook named "example"
â¯ nb notebooks author example
Current configuration for: example
--------------------------
email (global): example@example.test
name  (global): Example Name

Update?  [y/N]
```

The updated author email and name applies to subsequent commits.

To use a different email and name from the beginning of a notebook's history, create the new notebook using [`nb notebooks add --author`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) or [`nb notebooks init --author`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-notebooks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-notebooks"} ğŸ“š Notebooks {#-notebooks}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nbÂ notebooks`](#notebooks),\ [`nbÂ archive`](#archive),\ [`nbÂ unarchive`](#unarchive),\ [`nbÂ use`](#use)^

You can create additional notebooks, each of which has its own version history.

Create a new notebook with [`nb notebooks add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks):

``` highlight
# add a notebook named example
nb notebooks add example
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) list the available notebooks above the list of notes:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
example Â· home
--------------
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
[1] Title One
```

Commands in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} run within the current notebook, and identifiers such as ids, filenames, and titles refer to notes within the current notebook. `nb edit 3`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, for example, tells `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} to [`edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) note with id `3`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} within the current notebook.

To switch to a different notebook, use [`nb use`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#use):

``` highlight
# switch to the notebook named "example"
nb use example
```

If you are in one notebook and you want to perform a command in a different notebook without switching to it, add the notebook name with a colon before the command name:

``` highlight
# add a new note in the notebook "example"
nb example:add

# add a new note in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb example:a

# show note 5 in the notebook "example"
nb example:show 5

# show note 5 in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb example:s 5

# edit note 12 in the notebook "example"
nb example:edit 12

# edit note 12 in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb example:e 12

# search for "example query" in the notebook "example"
nb example:search "example query"

# search for "example query" in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb example:q "example query"

# show the revision history of the notebook "example"
nb example:history
```

The notebook name with colon can also be used as a modifier to the id, filename, or title:

``` highlight
# edit note 12 in the notebook "example"
nb edit example:12

# edit note 12 in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb e example:12

# edit note 12 in the notebook "example", alternative
nb example:12 edit

# edit note 12 in the notebook "example", alternative, shortcut alias
nb example:12 e

# show note titled "misc" in the notebook "example"
nb show example:misc

# show note titled "misc" in the notebook "example", shortcut alias
nb s example:misc

# delete note with filename "todos.md" in the notebook "example", alternative
nb example:todos.md delete

# delete note with filename "todos.md" in the notebook "example", alternative,
# shortcut alias
nb example:todos.md d
```

When a notebook name with colon is called without a subcommand, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} runs [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) in the specified notebook:

``` highlight
â¯ nb example:
example Â· home
--------------
[example:3] Title Three
[example:2] Title Two
[example:1] Title One
```

A bookmark can be created in another notebook by specifying the notebook name with colon, then a space, then the URL and bookmark options:

``` highlight
# create a new bookmark in a notebook named "sample"
â¯ nb sample: https://example.com --tags tag1,tag2
```

Notes can also be moved between notebooks:

``` highlight
# move note 3 from the current notebook to "example"
nb move 3 example:

# move note 5 in the notebook "example" to the notebook "sample"
nb move example:5 sample:
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#example-workflow){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="example-workflow"} Example Workflow

The flexibility of `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}'s argument handling makes it easy to build commands step by step as items are listed, filtered, viewed, and edited, particularly in combination with shell history:

``` highlight
# list items in the "example" notebook
â¯ nb example:
example Â· home
--------------
[example:3] Title Three
[example:2] Title Two
[example:1] Title One

# filter list
â¯ nb example: three
[example:3] Title Three

# view item
â¯ nb example:3 show
# opens item in `less`

# edit item
â¯ nb example:3 edit
# opens item in $EDITOR
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#notebooks-and-tab-completion){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="notebooks-and-tab-completion"} Notebooks and Tab Completion

[`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} tab completion](#tab-completion) is optimized for frequently running commands in various notebooks using the colon syntax, so installing the completion scripts is recommended and makes working with notebooks easy, fluid, and fun.

For example, listing the contents of a notebook is usually as simple as typing the first two or three characters of the name, then pressing the `<tab>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} key, then pressing `<enter>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} / `<return>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
â¯ nb exa<tab>
# completes to "example:"
â¯ nb example:
example Â· home
--------------
[example:3] Title Three
[example:2] Title Two
[example:1] Title One
```

Scoped notebook commands are also available in tab completion:

``` highlight
â¯ nb exa<tab>
# completes to "example:"
â¯ nb example:hi<tab>
# completes to "example:history"
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#notebooks-tags-and-taxonomy){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="notebooks-tags-and-taxonomy"} Notebooks, Tags, and Taxonomy

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is optimized to work well with a collection of notebooks, so notebooks are a good way to organize notes and bookmarks by top-level topic.

[#tags](#-tagging) are searchable across notebooks and can be created ad hoc, making notebooks and tags distinct and complementary organizational systems in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}.

Search for a tag in or across notebooks with [`nb search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search) / [`nb q`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search):

``` highlight
# search for #tag in the current notebook
nb q --tag tag

# search for #tag in all notebooks, short options
nb q -t tag -a

# search for #tag in the "example" notebook, argument
nb q example: "#tag"
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#global-and-local-notebooks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="global-and-local-notebooks"} Global and Local Notebooks

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#global-notebooks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="global-notebooks"} Global Notebooks

By default, all `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} notebooks are global, making them always accessible in the terminal regardless of the current working directory. Global notebooks are stored in the directory configured in [`nb set nb_dir`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_dir), which is `~/.nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} by default.

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#local-notebooks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="local-notebooks"} Local Notebooks

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also supports creating and working with local notebooks. Local notebooks are notebooks that are anywhere on the system outside of [`$NB_DIR`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_dir-1). Any folder can be an `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} local notebook, which is just a normal folder that has been initialized as a git repository and contains an `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} .index file. Initializing a folder as an `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} local notebook is a very easy way to add structured git versioning to any folder of documents and other files.

When `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} runs within a local notebook, the local notebook is set as the current notebook:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
local Â· example Â· home
----------------------
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
[1] Title One
```

A local notebook is always referred to by the name `local`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and otherwise behaves just like a global notebook whenever a command is run from within it:

``` highlight
# add a new note in the local notebook
nb add

# edit note 15 in the local notebook
nb edit 15

# move note titled "Todos" from the home notebook to the local notebook
nb move home:Todos local:

# move note 1 from the local notebook to the home notebook
nb move 1 home:

# search the local notebook for <query string>
nb search "query string"

# search the local notebook and all unarchived global notebooks for <query string>
nb search "query string" --all
```

Local notebooks can be created with [`nb notebooks init`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks):

``` highlight
# initialize the current directory as a notebook
nb notebooks init

# create a new notebook at ~/example
nb notebooks init ~/example

# clone an existing notebook to ~/example
nb notebooks init ~/example https://github.com/example/example.git
```

Local notebooks can also be created by exporting a global notebook:

``` highlight
# export global notebook named "example" to "../path/to/destination"
nb notebooks export example ../path/to/destination

# alternative
nb export example ../path/to/destination
```

Local notebooks can also be imported, making them global:

``` highlight
# import notebook or folder at "../path/to/notebook"
nb notebooks import ../path/to/notebook

# alternative
nb import ../path/to/notebook
```

[`nb notebooks init`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) and [`nb notebooks import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) can be used together to easily turn any directory of existing files into a global `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} notebook:

``` highlight
â¯ ls
example-directory

â¯ nb notebooks init example-directory
Initialized local notebook: /home/username/example-directory
```
