``` highlight
â¯ nb notebooks import example-directory
Imported notebook: example-directory

â¯ nb notebooks
example-directory
home
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#archiving-notebooks){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="archiving-notebooks"} Archiving Notebooks

^[â†‘](#-notebooks)\ Â·\ [`nbÂ archive`](#archive),\ [`nbÂ status`](#status),\ [`nbÂ unarchive`](#unarchive)^

Notebooks can be archived using [`nb archive`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#archive) (shortcut: [`nb ar`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#archive)):

``` highlight
# archive the current notebook
nb archive

# archive the notebook named "example"
nb archive example

# archive the current notebook, shortcut alias
nb ar

# archive the notebook named "example", shortcut alias
nb ar example
```

When a notebook is archived it is not included in [`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) / [`nb ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls) output, [`nb search --all`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search), or tab completion, nor synced automatically with [`nb sync --all`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#sync).

``` highlight
â¯ nb
example1 Â· example2 Â· example3 Â· [1 archived]
---------------------------------------------
[3] Title Three
[2] Title Two
[1] Title One
```

Archived notebooks can still be used individually using normal notebook commands:

``` highlight
# switch the current notebook to the archived notebook "example"
nb use example

# run the `list` subcommand in the archived notebook "example"
nb example:list
```

Check a notebook's archival status with [`nb status`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#status) (shortcut: [`nb st`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#status)) and [`nb notebooks status`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks):

``` highlight
# print status information, including archival status, for the current notebook
nb status

# print status information, including archival status, for the notebook named "example"
nb status example

# print status information, including archival status, for the current notebook,
# shortcut alias
nb st

# print status information, including archival status, for the notebook named "example",
# shortcut alias
nb st example

# print the archival status of the current notebook
nb notebooks status

# print the archival status of the notebook named "example"
nb notebooks status example
```

Use [`nb unarchive`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#unarchive) (shortcut: [`nb unar`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#unarchive)) to unarchive a notebook:

``` highlight
# unarchive the current notebook
nb unarchive

# unarchive the notebook named "example"
nb unarchive example
```

For more information about working with notebooks, see [`nb help notebooks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks), [`nb help archive`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#archive), and [`nb help unarchive`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#unarchive).

For technical details about notebooks, see [`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Notebook Specification](#nb-notebook-specification).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-git-sync){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-git-sync"} ğŸ”„ Git Sync {#-git-sync}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb remote`](#remote),\ [`nb sync`](#sync)^

Each notebook can be synced with a remote git repository by setting the remote URL using [`nb remote`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#remote):

``` highlight
# set the current notebook's remote to a private GitHub repository
nb remote set https://github.com/example/example

# set the remote for the notebook named "example"
nb example:remote set https://github.com/example/example
```

Any notebook with a remote URL will sync automatically every time a command is run in that notebook.

When you use `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} on multiple systems, you can set a notebook on each system to the same remote and `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} will keep everything in sync in the background every time there's a change in that notebook.

Since each notebook has its own git history, you can have some notebooks syncing with remotes while other notebooks are only available locally on that system.

Many services provide free private git repositories, so git syncing with `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is easy, free, and vendor-independent. You can also sync your notes using Dropbox, Drive, Box, Syncthing, or another syncing tool by changing your `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} directory with [`nb set nb_dir <path>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb_dir), and git syncing will still work simultaneously.

Clone an existing notebook by passing the URL to [`nb notebooks add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks):

``` highlight
# create a new notebook named "example" cloned from a private GitLab repository
nb notebooks add example https://gitlab.com/example/example.git
```

Turn off syncing for a notebook by removing the remote:

``` highlight
# remove the remote from the current notebook
nb remote remove

# remove the remote from the notebook named "example"
nb example:remote remove
```

Automatic git syncing can be turned on or off with [`nb set auto_sync`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#auto_sync).

To sync manually, use [`nb sync`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#sync):

``` highlight
# manually sync the current notebook
nb sync

# manually sync the notebook named "example"
nb example:sync
```

To bypass `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} syncing and run `git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} commands directly within a notebook, use [`nb git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#git):

``` highlight
# run `git fetch` in the current notebook
nb git fetch origin

# run `git status` in the notebook named "example"
nb example:git status
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#syncing-multiple-notebooks-with-one-remote){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="syncing-multiple-notebooks-with-one-remote"} Syncing Multiple Notebooks with One Remote

Multiple notebooks can be synced to one remote using orphan branches. An [orphan branch](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-checkout#Documentation/git-checkout.txt---orphanltnewbranchgt) is a branch with a history that is independent from the repository's `main`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `master`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, or equivalent primary branch history. To sync a notebook with a new orphan branch, add the remote using [`nb remote set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#remote) and select the option to create a new orphan branch. The name of orphan branch is derived from notebook name and can alternatively be specified as an argument to [`nb remote set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#remote):

``` highlight
# set the remote for the current notebook to a remote URL and branch
nb remote set https://github.com/xwmx/example demo-branch
```

To create a notebook using an existing orphan branch on a remote, pass the branch name to [`nb init`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#init), [`nb notebooks add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks), or [`nb notebooks init`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) after the URL:

``` highlight
# initialize new "home" notebook with the branch "sample-branch" on the remote
nb init https://github.com/xwmx/example sample-branch

# add a new "example" notebook from the branch "example-branch" on the remote
nb notebooks add example https://github.com/xwmx/example example-branch
```

To list all branches on a remote, use [`nb remote branches`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#remote):

``` highlight
# list all branches on the current remote
nb remote branches

# list all branches on a remote repository identified by a URL
nb remote branches "https://github.com/xwmx/example"
```

For information about assigning remotes, see [`nb help remote`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#remote).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#private-repositories-and-git-credentials){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="private-repositories-and-git-credentials"} Private Repositories and Git Credentials

Syncing with private repositories requires configuring git to not prompt for credentials. For repositories cloned over HTTPS, [credentials can be cached with git](https://docs.github.com/en/free-pro-team@latest/github/using-git/caching-your-github-credentials-in-git) . For repositories cloned over SSH, [keys can be added to the ssh-agent](https://docs.github.com/en/free-pro-team@latest/github/authenticating-to-github/generating-a-new-ssh-key-and-adding-it-to-the-ssh-agent) .

Use [`nb sync`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#sync) within a notebook to determine whether your configuration is working. If `nb sync`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} displays a password prompt, then follow the instructions above to configure your credentials. The password prompt can be used to authenticate, but `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} does not cache or otherwise handle git credentials in any way, so there will likely be multiple password prompts during each sync if credentials are not configured.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#sync-conflict-resolution){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="sync-conflict-resolution"} Sync Conflict Resolution

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} handles git operations automatically, so you shouldn't ever need to use the `git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} command line tool directly. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} merges changes when syncing and handles conflicts using a couple different strategies.

When [`nb sync`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#sync) encounters a conflict in a text file and can't cleanly merge overlapping local and remote changes, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} saves both versions within the file separated by git conflict markers and prints a message indicating which files contain conflicting text. Use [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) to remove the conflict markers and delete any unwanted text.

For example, in the following file, the second list item was changed on two systems, and git has no way to determine which one we want to keep:

``` highlight
# Example Title

- List Item apple
<<<<<<< HEAD
- List Item apricot
=======
- List Item pluot
>>>>>>> 719od01... [nb] Commit
- List Item plum
```

The local change is between the lines starting with `<<<<<<<`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `=======`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, while the remote change is between the `=======`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and `>>>>>>>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} lines.

To resolve this conflict by keeping both items, simply edit the file with [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) and remove the lines starting with `<<<<<<<`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, `=======`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, and `>>>>>>>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}:

``` highlight
# Example Title

- List Item apple
- List Item apricot
- List Item pluot
- List Item plum
```

When `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} encounters a conflict in a binary file, such as an encrypted note, both versions of the file are saved in the notebook as individual files, with `--conflicted-copy`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} appended to the filename of the version from the remote. To resolve a conflicted copy of a binary file, compare both versions and merge them manually, then delete the `--conflicted-copy`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}.

If you do encounter a conflict that `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} says it can't merge at all, [`nb git`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#git) and [`nb run`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#run) can be used to perform git and shell operations within the notebook to resolve the conflict manually. Please also [open an issue](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/issues/new) with any relevant details that could inform a strategy for handling any such cases automatically.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#ï¸-import--export){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="ï¸-import--export"} â†•ï¸ Import / Export {#ï¸-import--export}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb import`](#import),\ [`nb export`](#export),\ [`nb browse`](#browse)^

Files of any type can be imported into a notebook using [`nb import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) (shortcut: [`nb i`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import)). [`nb edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit) and [`nb open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open) open files in your system's default application for that file type.

``` highlight
# import an image file
nb import ~/Pictures/example.png

# open image in your default image viewer
nb open example.png

# import a .docx file
nb import ~/Documents/example.docx

# open .docx file in Word or your system's .docx viewer
nb open example.docx
```

Multiple filenames and globbing are supported:

``` highlight
# import all files and directories in the current directory
nb import ./*

# import all markdown files in the current directory
nb import ./*.md

# import example.md and sample.md in the current directory
nb import example.md sample.md
```

[`nb import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) can also download and import files directly from the web:

``` highlight
# import a PDF file from the web
nb import https://example.com/example.pdf
# Imported "https://example.com/example.pdf" to "example.pdf"

# open example.pdf in your system's PDF viewer
nb open example.pdf
```

Some imported file types have [indicators](#indicators) to make them easier to identify in lists:

``` highlight
â¯ nb
home
----
[6] ğŸ“– example-ebook.epub
[5] ğŸŒ„ example-picture.png
[4] ğŸ“„ example-document.docx
[3] ğŸ“¹ example-video.mp4
[2] ğŸ”‰ example-audio.mp3
[1] ğŸ“‚ Example Folder
```

Notes, bookmarks, and other files can be exported using [`nb export`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export). If [Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/) is installed, notes can be automatically converted to any of the [formats supported by Pandoc](https://pandoc.org/MANUAL.html#option--to). By default, the output format is determined by the file extension:

``` highlight
# export a Markdown note to a .docx Microsoft Office Word document
nb export example.md /path/to/example.docx

# export a note titled "Movies" to an HTML web page.
nb export Movies /path/to/example.html
```

For more control over the `pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} options, use the [`nb export pandoc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export) subcommand:

``` highlight
# export note 42 as an epub with pandoc options
nb export pandoc 42 --from markdown_strict --to epub -o path/to/example.epub
```

[`nb export notebook`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export) and [`nb import notebook`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) can be used to export and import notebooks:

``` highlight
# export global notebook named "example" to "../path/to/destination"
nb export notebook example ../path/to/destination

# import notebook or folder at "../path/to/notebook"
nb import notebook ../path/to/notebook
```

[`nb export notebook`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export) and [`nb import notebook`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) behave like aliases for [`nb notebooks export`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) and [`nb notebooks import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks), and the subcommands can be used interchangeably.

For more information about imported and exported notebooks, see [Global and Local Notebooks](#global-and-local-notebooks).

For [`nb import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) and [`nb export`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export) help information, see [`nb help import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import) and [`nb help export`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#export).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#exporting-with-browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="exporting-with-browse"} Exporting with `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

Items can be exported using terminal and GUI [web browsers](#-browsing). Use the down arrow (`â†“`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}) link on the [`nb browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse) item page to download the original file:

``` highlight
â¯ nb browse 123
â¯nb Â· home : 123 Â· â†“ | +

    example.pdf
Â 
```

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#ï¸-set--settings){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="ï¸-set--settings"} âš™ï¸ `set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} & `settings`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} {#ï¸-set--settings}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [Variables](#-variables),\ [`nb settings`](#settings),\ [`nb unset`](#unset)^

[`nb set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) and [`nb settings`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) open the settings prompt, which provides an easy way to change your `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} settings.

``` highlight
nb set
```

To update a setting in the prompt, enter the setting name or number and then enter the new value. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} will add the setting to your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} configuration file.

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#example-editor){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="example-editor"} Example: editor

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} can be configured to use a specific command line editor using the `editor`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} setting.

The settings prompt for a setting can be started by passing the setting name or number to [`nb set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings):

``` highlight
â¯ nb set editor
[6]  editor
     ------
     The command line text editor used by `nb`.

     â€¢Â Example Values:

         atom
         code
         emacs
         macdown
         mate
         micro
         nano
         pico
         subl
         vi
         vim

EDITOR is currently set to vim

Enter a new value, unset to set to the default value, or q to quit.
Value:
```

A setting can also be updated without the prompt by passing both the name and value to [`nb set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings):

``` highlight
# set editor with setting name
â¯ nb set editor code
EDITOR set to code

# set editor with setting number (6)
â¯ nb set 6 code
EDITOR set to code

# set the color theme to blacklight
â¯ nb set color_theme blacklight
NB_COLOR_THEME set to blacklight

# set the default `ls` limit to 10
â¯ nb set limit 10
NB_LIMIT set to 10
```

Use [`nb settings get`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) to print the value of a setting:

``` highlight
â¯ nb settings get editor
code

â¯ nb settings get 6
code
```

Use [`nb unset`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#unset) or [`nb settings unset`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) to unset a setting and revert to the default:

``` highlight
â¯ nb unset editor
EDITOR restored to the default: vim

â¯ nb settings get editor
vim
```

[`nb set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) and [`nb settings`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) are aliases that refer to the same subcommand, so the two subcommand names can be used interchangeably.

For more information about [`set`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings) and [`settings`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings), see [`nb help settings`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings).

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-color-themes){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-color-themes"} ğŸ¨ Color Themes {#-color-themes}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nbÂ setÂ color_theme`](#color_theme),\ [`nbÂ setÂ syntax_theme`](#syntax_theme),\ [`nbÂ setÂ color_primary`](#color_primary),\ [`nbÂ setÂ color_secondary`](#color_secondary)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} uses color to highlight various interface elements, including ids and [selectors](#-selectors), the current notebook name, the shell prompt, divider lines, [syntax elements](#terminal-syntax-highlighting-theme), and links.

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes several built-in color themes and also supports user-defined themes. The current color theme can be set using [`nb set color_theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#color_theme):

``` highlight
nb set color_theme
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#built-in-color-themes){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="built-in-color-themes"} Built-in Color Themes

   ![utility](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-theme-utility-home.png)   ![utility](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-theme-utility-web.png)
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
                                        Â                                                                             Â 

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#custom-color-themes){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="custom-color-themes"} Custom Color Themes

Color themes are [`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} plugins](#-plugins) with a `.nb-theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file extension. `.nb-theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files are expected to contain one `if`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} statement testing for the theme name and setting the color environment variables to `tput`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} ANSI color numbers:

``` highlight
# turquoise.nb-theme
if [[ "${NB_COLOR_THEME}" == "turquoise" ]]
then
  export NB_COLOR_PRIMARY=43
  export NB_COLOR_SECONDARY=38
fi
```

View this theme as a complete file: [`plugins/turquoise.nb-theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/turquoise.nb-theme)

Themes can be installed using [`nb plugins`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins):

``` highlight
â¯ nb plugins install https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/turquoise.nb-theme
Plugin installed:
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/turquoise.nb-theme
```

Once a theme is installed, use [`nb set color_theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#color_theme) to set it as the current theme:

``` highlight
â¯ nb set color_theme turquoise
NB_COLOR_THEME set to turquoise
```

The primary and secondary colors can also be overridden individually, making color themes easily customizable:

``` highlight
# open the settings prompt for the primary color
nb set color_primary

# open the settings prompt for the secondary color
nb set color_secondary
```

To view a table of available colors and numbers, run:

``` highlight
nb set colors
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#terminal-syntax-highlighting-theme){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="terminal-syntax-highlighting-theme"} Terminal Syntax Highlighting Theme

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} displays files with syntax highlighting when [`bat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/sharkdp/bat), [`highlight`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](http://www.andre-simon.de/doku/highlight/en/highlight.php), or [Pygments](https://pygments.org/) is installed.

When `bat`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is installed, syntax highlighting color themes are available for both light and dark terminal backgrounds. To view a list of available themes and set the syntax highlighting color theme, use [`nb set syntax_theme`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#syntax_theme).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#gui-web-syntax-highlighting){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="gui-web-syntax-highlighting"} GUI Web Syntax Highlighting

Syntax highlighting is also available when viewing and editing items in text formats with [`nb browse --gui`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse---gui), which incorporates the color theme's primary color into the syntax theme:

![nb syntax highlighting](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/nb-web-pandoc-ruby-utility.png){width="500"}

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#indicators){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="indicators"} Indicators

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} uses emoji characters to represent information about files in lists. These characters are referred to internally as "indicators" and can be customized by assigning a different character to the indicator's environment variable in your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file, which can be opened with [`nb settings edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#settings).

For example, to use a different indicator for pinned items, add a line like the following to your `~/.nbrc`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} file:

``` highlight
export NB_INDICATOR_PINNED="âœ¨"
```

To turn off an indicator, assign the variable to an empty string:

``` highlight
export NB_INDICATOR_PINNED=""
```

Available indicator [variables](#-variables) with default values:

``` highlight
export  NB_INDICATOR_AUDIO="ğŸ”‰"
export  NB_INDICATOR_BOOKMARK="ğŸ”–"
export  NB_INDICATOR_DOCUMENT="ğŸ“„"
export  NB_INDICATOR_EBOOK="ğŸ“–"
export  NB_INDICATOR_ENCRYPTED="ğŸ”’"
export  NB_INDICATOR_FOLDER="ğŸ“‚"
export  NB_INDICATOR_IMAGE="ğŸŒ„"
export  NB_INDICATOR_PINNED="ğŸ“Œ"
export  NB_INDICATOR_TODO="âœ”ï¸ "
export  NB_INDICATOR_TODO_DONE="âœ…"
export  NB_INDICATOR_VIDEO="ğŸ“¹"
```

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-shell-theme-support){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-shell-theme-support"} \$ Shell Theme Support {#-shell-theme-support}

-   [`astral`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Zsh Theme](https://github.com/xwmx/astral) - Displays the current notebook name in the context line of the prompt.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-plugins){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-plugins"} ğŸ”Œ Plugins {#-plugins}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [Plugin\ Help](#plugin-help),\ [`nb plugins`](#plugins)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes support for plugins, which can be used to create new subcommands, design themes, and otherwise extend the functionality of `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}.

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} supports two types of plugins, identified by their file extensions:

`.nb-theme`
:   Plugins defining [color themes](#custom-color-themes).

`.nb-plugin`
:   Plugins defining new subcommands and adding functionality.

Plugins are managed with the [`nb plugins`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins) subcommand and are installed in the `${NB_DIR}/.plugins`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} directory.

Plugins can be installed from either a URL or a path using the [`nb plugins install`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins) subcommand.

``` highlight
# install a plugin from a URL
nb plugins install https://raw.githubusercontent.com/xwmx/nb/master/plugins/clip.nb-plugin

# install a plugin from a standard GitHub URL
nb plugins install https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/example.nb-plugin

# install a theme from a standard GitHub URL
nb plugins install https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/turquoise.nb-theme

# install a plugin from a path
nb plugins install plugins/example.nb-plugin
```

The `<url>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} should be the full URL to the plugin file. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also recognizes regular GitHub URLs, which can be used interchangeably with raw GitHub URLs.

Installed plugins can be listed with [`nb plugins`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins), which optionally takes a name and prints full paths:

``` highlight
â¯ nb plugins
clip.nb-plugin
example.nb-plugin
turquoise.nb-theme

â¯ nb plugins clip.nb-plugin
clip.nb-plugin

â¯ nb plugins --paths
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/clip.nb-plugin
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/example.nb-plugin
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/turquoise.nb-theme

â¯ nb plugins turquoise.nb-theme --paths
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/turquoise.nb-theme
```

Use [`nb plugins uninstall`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins) to uninstall a plugin:

``` highlight
â¯ nb plugins uninstall example.nb-plugin
Plugin successfully uninstalled:
/home/example/.nb/.plugins/example.nb-plugin
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#creating-plugins){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="creating-plugins"} Creating Plugins

Plugins are written in a Bash-compatible shell scripting language and have an `.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} extension.

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes a few example plugins:

-   [`example.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/example.nb-plugin)
-   [`clip.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/clip.nb-plugin)
-   [`ebook.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/ebook.nb-plugin)

Create a new subcommand in three easy steps:

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#1-add-the-new-subcommand-name-with-_subcommands-add-name){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="1-add-the-new-subcommand-name-with-_subcommands-add-name"} 1. Add the new subcommand name with `_subcommands add <name>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}: {#1-add-the-new-subcommand-name-with-_subcommands-add-name}

``` highlight
_subcommands add "example"
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#2-define-help-and-usage-text-with-_subcommands-describe-subcommand-usage){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="2-define-help-and-usage-text-with-_subcommands-describe-subcommand-usage"} 2. Define help and usage text with `_subcommands describe <subcommand> <usage>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}: {#2-define-help-and-usage-text-with-_subcommands-describe-subcommand-usage}

``` highlight
_subcommands describe "example" <<HEREDOC
Usage:
  nb example

Description:
  Print "Hello, World!"
HEREDOC
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#3-define-the-subcommand-as-a-function-named-with-a-leading-underscore){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="3-define-the-subcommand-as-a-function-named-with-a-leading-underscore"} 3. Define the subcommand as a function, named with a leading underscore: {#3-define-the-subcommand-as-a-function-named-with-a-leading-underscore}

``` highlight
_example() {
  printf "Hello, World!\\n"
}
```

That's it! ğŸ‰

View the complete plugin: [`plugins/example.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/example.nb-plugin)

With `example.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} installed, `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} includes an `nb example`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} subcommand that prints "Hello, World!"

For a full example, [`clip.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/clip.nb-plugin) add clipboard functionality to `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} and demonstrates how to create a plugin using `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} subcommands and simple shell scripting.

You can install any plugin you create locally with [`nb plugins install <path>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins), and you can publish it on GitHub, GitLab, or anywhere else online and install it with [`nb plugins install <url>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#plugins).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#api){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="api"} API

The `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} API is the [command line interface](#nb-help), which is designed for composability and provides a variety of powerful options for interacting with notes, bookmarks, notebooks, and `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} functionality. Within plugins, subcommands can be called using their function names, which are named with leading underscores. Options can be used to output information in formats suitable for parsing and processing:

``` highlight
# print the content of note 3 to standard output with no color
_show 3 --print --no-color

# list all unarchived global notebook names
_notebooks --names --no-color --unarchived --global

# list all filenames in the current notebook
_list --filenames --no-id --no-indicator

# print the path to the current notebook
_notebooks current --path
```

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} automatically scans arguments for [selectors](#-selectors) with notebook names and updates the current notebook if a valid one is found.

Identifier selectors are passed to subcommands as arguments along with any subcommand options. Use [`show <selector>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) to query information about the file specified in the selector. For example, to obtain the filename of a selector-specified file, use [`show <selector> --filename`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show):

``` highlight
_example() {
  local _selector="${1:-}"
  [[ -z "${_selector:-}" ]] && printf "Usage: example <selector>\\n" && exit 1

  # Get the filename using the selector.
  local _filename=
  _filename="$(_show "${_selector}" --filename)"

  # Rest of subcommand function...
}
```

[`notebooks current --path`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) returns the path to the current notebook:

``` highlight
# _example() continued:

# get the notebook path
local _notebook_path=
_notebook_path="$(_notebooks current --path)"

# print the file at "${_notebook_path}/${_filename}" to standard output
cat "${_notebook_path}/${_filename}"
```

See [`clip.nb-plugin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://github.com/xwmx/nb/blob/master/plugins/clip.nb-plugin) for a practical example using both [`show <selector>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) and [`notebooks current --path`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#notebooks) along with other subcommands called using their underscore-prefixed function names.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-selectors){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-selectors"} `:/`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Selectors {#-selectors}

^[â†‘](#overview)^

Items in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} are primarily identified using structured arguments called "selectors." Selectors are like addresses for notebooks, folders, and items. A selector can be as simple as an id like `123`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} or folder path like `example/`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}, or it can combine multiple elements to identify an item in a nested folder within a particular notebook, such as:

``` highlight
cli:tools/shellcheck/home-page.bookmark.md
```

An item, folder, or notebook selector is constructed by specifying the notebook name, folder path, and / or item identifier in the following pattern:

``` highlight
notebook:folder/path/item-idenitifer
```

Represented in a [docopt](http://docopt.org/)-like format:

``` highlight
[<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>]
```

Notebooks are identified by the notebook name followed by a colon. Folder and item identifiers without a notebook name refer to items within the current notebook. When a selector consists of notebook name and colon with no folder path or item identifer, the command runs in the root folder of the notebook:

``` highlight
# list items in the "example" notebook
nb example:

# add a new note named "Example Title" to the "example" notebook
nb add example: --title "Example Title"

# edit item with id "123" in the notebook "example"
nb edit example:123
```

A notebook selector can be combined with a subcommand name to run the command within the notebook:

``` highlight
# list all items in the "example" notebook and display excerpts
nb example:list -e

# edit item with id "123" in the "example" notebook
nb example:edit 123

# show the git history for the notebook named "example"
nb example:history
```

Folders are identified by relative path from the notebook root. Folders can be referenced by either id or name, and segments in nested paths can mix and match names and ids:

``` highlight
# list items in the folder named "sample" in the folder named demo"
nb sample/demo/

# add a new item to the folder named "demo" in the folder with id "3"
nb add 3/demo/

# show the history of the folder with id "4" in the folder named
# "sample" in the notebook named "example"
nb history example:sample/4/
```

A trailing slash indicates that the command is expected to operate on the contents of the folder. When a trailing slash is omitted, the selector refers to the folder itself:

``` highlight
â¯ nb list sample
[1] ğŸ“‚ sample

â¯ nb list sample/
[sample/3] Title Three
[sample/2] Title Two
[sample/1] Title One
```

For more information about folders, see [Folders](#-folders).

An item is identified by id, filename, or title, optionally preceeded by notebook name or folder path:

``` highlight
# edit item with id "123"
nb edit 123

# open the item titled "demo title" in the folder with id "3"
nb open 3/demo\ title

# show "file.md" in the "sample" folder in the "example" notebook
nb show example:sample/file.md
```

Items can also be specified using the full path:

``` highlight
# edit "demo.md" in the "sample" folder in the "home" notebook
nb edit /home/example/.nb/home/sample/demo.md
```

##### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#examples){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="examples"} Examples

*Idenitifer Selectors*

``` highlight
123
example.md
title
relative/path/to/123
relative/path/to/demo.md
relative/path/to/title
/full/path/to/sample.md
notebook:123
notebook:example.md
notebook:title
notebook:relative/path/to/123
notebook:relative/path/to/demo.md
notebook:relative/path/to/title
```

*Subcommand Selectors*

``` highlight
notebook:
notebook:show
notebook:history
notebook:a
notebook:q
```

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#01-metadata){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="01-metadata"} `01`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Metadata {#01-metadata}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb show`](#show)^

Metadata in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} is primarily derived from git, the filesystem, and file content. For example, displayed timestamps are derived from [`git log`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-log), with [`nb show --added`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) displaying the datetime of the first commit containing the file and [`nb show --updated`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show) displaying the datetime of the last commit in which the file was modified. Meanwhile, the file system's modified timestamp is used for sorting.

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} also uses plain text files to store ids and state information in git, including [`.index`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files](https://github.com/xwmx/nb#index-files), [`.pindex`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files](https://github.com/xwmx/nb#pindex-files), and [`.archived`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} files](https://github.com/xwmx/nb#archived-notebooks).

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#front-matter){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="front-matter"} Front Matter

User-defined metadata can be added to notes in `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} using [front matter](https://jekyllrb.com/docs/front-matter/). Front matter is a simple, human accessible, and future-friendly method for defining metadata fields in plain text and is well supported in tools for working with Markdown.

Front matter is defined within a Markdown file with triple-dashed lines (`---`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}) indicating the start and end of the block, with each field represented by a key name with a colon followed by the value:

``` highlight
---
title:  Example Title
author: xwmx
year:   2021
---

Example content.

More example content:

- one
- two
- three
```

Any metadata can be placed in the front matter block. `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} uses the `title:`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} field for listing, filtering, and selecting items, if one is present, and ignores any other fields.

The simple `key: value`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} syntax is suitable for many metadata fields. More complex data can be defined using additional [YAML](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YAML) capabilities.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-interactive-shell){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-interactive-shell"} `â¯`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Interactive Shell {#-interactive-shell}

^[â†‘](#overview)\ Â·\ [`nb shell`](#shell)^

`nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} has an interactive shell that can be started with [`nb shell`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#shell), [`nb -i`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help), or [`nb --interactive`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help):

``` highlight
$ nb shell
__          _
\ \   _ __ | |__
 \ \ | '_ \| '_ \
 / / | | | | |_) |
/_/  |_| |_|_.__/
------------------
nb shell started. Enter ls to list notes and notebooks.
Enter help for usage information. Enter exit to exit.
nbâ¯ ls
home
----
[3] Example
[2] Sample
[1] Demo

nbâ¯ edit 3 --content "New content."
Updated: [3] Example

nbâ¯ bookmark https://example.com
Added: [4] ğŸ”– example.bookmark.md "Example Title (example.com)"

nbâ¯ ls
home
----
[4] ğŸ”– Example Title (example.com)
[3] Example
[2] Sample
[1] Demo

nbâ¯ bookmark url 4
https://example.com

nbâ¯ search "example"
[4] example.bookmark.md "Example (example.com)"
-----------------------------------------------
1:# Example (example.com)

3:<https://example.com>

[3] example.md "Example"
------------------------
1:# Example

nbâ¯ exit
$
```

The `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} shell recognizes all `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} subcommands and options, providing a streamlined, distraction-free approach for working with `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}.

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#shortcut-aliases){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="shortcut-aliases"} Shortcut Aliases

^[â†‘](#overview)^

Several core `nb`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} subcommands have shortcut aliases to make them faster to work with:

``` highlight
# `a` (add): add a new note named "example.md"
nb a example.md

# `+` (add): add a new note titled "Example Title"
nb + --title "Example Title"

# `b` (browse): open the folder named "sample" in the web browser
nb b sample/

# `o` (open): open the URL from bookmark 12 in your web browser
nb o 12

# `p` (peek): open the URL from bookmark 6 in your terminal browser
nb p 6

# `e` (edit): edit note 5
nb e 5

# `d` (delete): delete note 19
nb d 19

# `d` (delete): delete note 123 in the notebook named "example:"
nb - example:123

# `s` (show): show note 27
nb s 27

# `q` (search): search notes for "example query"
nb q "example query"

# `h` (help): display the help information for the `add` subcommand
nb h add

# `u` (use): switch to example-notebook
nb u example-notebook
```

For more commands and options, run [`nb help`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#nb-help) or [`nb help <subcommand>`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#subcommands)

![nb browse themes](https://xwmx.github.io/misc/nb/images/gui-browse-themes.png){width="700"}

### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#-help){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="-help"} `?`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge} Help {#-help}

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#nb-help){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="nb-help"} `nb help`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [`help`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#help)

``` highlight
__          _
\ \   _ __ | |__
 \ \ | '_ \| '_ \
 / / | | | | |_) |
/_/  |_| |_|_.__/

[nb] Command line and local web note-taking, bookmarking, and archiving with
plain text data storage, encryption, filtering and search, pinning, #tagging,
Git-backed versioning and syncing, Pandoc-backed conversion, global and local
notebooks, customizable color themes, [[wiki-style linking]], plugins, and more
in a single portable, user-friendly script.

Help:
  nb help               Display this help information.
  nb help <subcommand>  View help information for <subcommand>.
  nb help --colors      View information about color settings.
  nb help --readme      View the `nb` README file.

Usage:
  nb
  nb [<ls-options>...] [<id> | <filename> | <path> | <title> | <notebook>]

  nb add [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<filename>] [<content>]
         [-b | --browse] [-c <content> | --content <content>] [--edit]

              [-r (<url> | <selector>) | --related (<url> | <selector>)]...
              [-t <tag1>,<tag2>... | --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...] [--title <title>]
  nb bookmark [list [<list-options>...]]

  nb bookmark (edit | delete) (<id> | <filename> | <path> | <title>)
  nb bookmark search <query>
  nb browse [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>]
            [-g | --gui] [-n | --notebooks] [-p | --print] [-q | --query <query>]

        [<task-number>]

          [-c <content> | --content <content>] [--edit]

            <path> [-f | --force] [<pandoc options>...]
  nb export notebook <name> [<path>]
  nb export pandoc ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
            [<pandoc options>...]

          [-n <limit> | --limit <limit> | --<limit>] [--no-id]

                 [open | closed]

          [<task-number>]

  nb unset (<name> | <number>)

  nb -h | --help | help [<subcommand> | --readme]
  nb -i | --interactive [<subcommand> [<options>...]]
  nb --no-color
  nb --version | version

Subcommands:
  (default)    List notes and notebooks. This is an alias for `nb ls`.
               When a <url> is provided, create a new bookmark.
  add          Add a note, folder, or file.
  archive      Archive the current or specified notebook.
  bookmark     Add, open, list, and search bookmarks.
  browse       Browse and manage linked items in terminal and GUI web browsers.
  completions  Install and uninstall completion scripts.
  copy         Copy or duplicate an item.
  count        Print the number of items in a notebook or folder.
  delete       Delete a note.
  do           Mark a todo or task as done.
  edit         Edit a note.
  export       Export a note to a variety of different formats.
  folders      Add, delete, and list folders.
  git          Run `git` commands within the current notebook.
  help         View help information for the program or a subcommand.
  history      View git history for the current notebook or a note.
  import       Import a file into the current notebook.
  init         Initialize the first notebook.
  list         List notes in the current notebook.
  ls           List notebooks and notes in the current notebook.
  move         Move or rename a note.
  notebooks    Manage notebooks.
  open         Open a bookmarked web page or notebook folder, or edit a note.
  peek         View a note, bookmarked web page, or notebook in the terminal.
  pin          Pin an item so it appears first in lists.
  plugins      Install and uninstall plugins and themes.
  remote       Configure the remote URL and branch for the notebook.
  run          Run shell commands within the current notebook.
  search       Search notes.
  settings     Edit configuration settings.
  shell        Start the `nb` interactive shell.
  show         Show a note or notebook.
  status       Run `git status` in the current notebook.
  subcommands  List, add, alias, and describe subcommands.
  status       Print notebook status information.
  sync         Sync local notebook with the remote repository.
  tasks        List tasks in todos, notebooks, folders, and other items.
  todo         Manage todos and tasks.
  unarchive    Unarchive the current or specified notebook.
  undo         Mark a todo or task as not done.
  unpin        Unpin a pinned item.
  unset        Return a setting to its default value.
  update       Update `nb` to the latest version.
  use          Switch to a notebook.
  version      Display version information.

Notebook Usage:
  nb <notebook>:[<subcommand>] [<identifier>] [<options>...]
  nb <subcommand> <notebook>:<identifier> [<options>...]

Program Options:
  -h, --help          Display this help information.
  -i, --interactive   Start the `nb` interactive shell.
  --no-color          Print without color highlighting.
  --version           Display version information.

More Information:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#bookmark-help){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="bookmark-help"} `bookmark help`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Bookmarks](#-bookmarks), [`bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark), [`browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse)

``` highlight
    __                __                        __
   / /_  ____  ____  / /______ ___  ____ ______/ /__
  / __ \/ __ \/ __ \/ //_/ __ `__ \/ __ `/ ___/ //_/
 / /_/ / /_/ / /_/ / ,< / / / / / / /_/ / /  / ,<
/_.___/\____/\____/_/|_/_/ /_/ /_/\__,_/_/  /_/|_|

bookmark -- Command line bookmarking with tagging, encryption,
full-text page content search with regular expression support,
GUI and terminal browser support, and data stored in plain text
Markdown files with Git-backed versioning and syncing.

Usage:
  bookmark [<ls-options>...]
  bookmark [<notebook>:][<folder-path>] <url>
              [-c <comment> | --comment <comment>] [--edit] [-e | --encrypt]
              [-f <filename> | --filename <filename>] [--no-request]
              [-q <quote> | --quote <quote>] [--save-source]
              [-r (<url> | <selector>) | --related (<url> | <selector>)]...
              [-t <tag1>,<tag2>... | --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...] [--title <title>]
  bookmark (edit | delete | open | peek | url)
              ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
  bookmark search <query>

Options:
  -c, --comment <comment>      A comment or description for this bookmark.
  --edit                       Open the bookmark in your editor before saving.
  -e, --encrypt                Encrypt the bookmark with a password.
  -f, --filename <filename>    The filename for the bookmark. It is
                               recommended to omit the extension so the
                               default bookmark extension is used.
  --no-request                 Don't request or download the target page.
  -q, --quote <quote>          A quote or excerpt from the saved page.
                               Alias: `--excerpt`
  -r, --related <selector>     A selector for an item related to the
                               bookmarked page.
  -r, --related <url>          A URL for a page related to the bookmarked page.
                               Multiple `--related` flags can be used in a
                               command to save multiple related URLs.
  --save-source                Save the page source as HTML.
  -t, --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...  A comma-separated list of tags.
  --title <title>              The bookmark title. When not specified,
                               `nb` will use the html <title> tag.

Subcommands:
  (default)  Add a new bookmark for <url>, or list bookmarks.
             Bookmarks can also be added with `nb <url>`
  delete     Delete a bookmark.
  edit       Edit a bookmark.
  list       List bookmarks in the current notebook.
             Shortcut Alias: `ls`
  open       Open the bookmarked page in your system's primary web browser.
             Shortcut Alias: `o`
  peek       Open the bookmarked page in your terminal web browser.
             Alias: `preview`
             Shortcut Alias: `p`
  search     Search bookmarks for <query>.
             Shortcut Alias: `q`
  url        Print the URL for the specified bookmark.

Description:
  Create, view, search, edit, and delete bookmarks.

  By default, the html page content is saved within the bookmark, making the
  bookmarked page available for full-text search. When Pandoc [1] is
  installed, the HTML content is converted to Markdown before saving.
  When readability-cli [2] is install, markup is cleaned up to focus on
  content.

  `peek` opens the page in `w3m` [3] or `links` [4] when available.
  To specify a preferred browser, set the `$BROWSER` environment variable
  in your .bashrc, .zshrc, or equivalent, e.g.: export BROWSER="lynx"

  Bookmarks are identified by the `.bookmark.md` file extension. The
  bookmark URL is the first URL in the file within "<" and ">" characters:

    <https://www.example.com>

    1. https://pandoc.org/
    2. https://gitlab.com/gardenappl/readability-cli
    3. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m
    4. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)

Read More:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb#-bookmarks

See Also:
  nb help browse
  nb help open
  nb help peek
  nb help show

Examples:
  bookmark https://example.com
  bookmark https://example.com --encrypt
  bookmark https://example.com --tags example,sample,demo
  bookmark https://example.com/about -c "Example comment."
  bookmark https://example.com/faqs -f example-filename
  bookmark https://example.com --quote "Example quote or excerpt."
  bookmark list
  bookmark search "example query"
  bookmark open 5

------------------------------------------
Part of `nb` (https://github.com/xwmx/nb).
For more information, see: `nb help`.
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#add){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="add"} `add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Adding](#adding), [`bookmark`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#bookmark), [`browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), [`delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete), [`edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit), [`folders`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#folders), [`import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import), [`show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show), [`todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo)

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb add [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<filename>] [<content>]
         [-b | --browse] [-c <content> | --content <content>] [--edit]
         [-e | --encrypt] [-f <filename> | --filename <filename>]
         [--folder <folder-path>] [--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...]
         [-t <title> | --title <title>] [--type <type>]
  nb add bookmark [<bookmark-options>...]
  nb add folder [<name>]
  nb add todo [<todo-options>...]

Options:
  -b, --browse                Add using a terminal or GUI web browser.
  -c, --content <content>     The content for the new note.
  --edit                      Open the note in the editor before saving when
                              content is piped or passed as an argument.
  -e, --encrypt               Encrypt the note with a password.
  -f, --filename <filename>   The filename for the new note.
  --folder <folder-path>      Add within the folder located at <folder-path>.
  --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...     A comma-separated list of tags.
  -t, --title <title>         The title for a new note. If `--title` is
                              present, the filename is derived from the
                              title, unless `--filename` is specified.
  --type <type>               The file type for the new note, as a file
                              extension.

Description:
  Create a new note or folder.

  If no arguments are passed, a new blank note file is opened with `$EDITOR`,
  currently set to: example

  If a non-option argument is passed, `nb` will treat it as a <filenameâ‰¥
  if a file extension is found. If no file extension is found,  `nb` will
  treat the string as <content> and will create a new note without opening the
  editor. `nb add` can also create a new note with piped content.

  `nb` creates Markdown files by default. To create a note with a
  different file type, use the extension in the filename or use the `--type`
  option. To change the default file type, use `nb set default_extension`.

  When the `-e` / `--encrypt` option is used, `nb` will encrypt the
  note with AES-256 using OpenSSL by default, or GPG, if configured in
  `nb set encryption_tool`.

Read More:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb#adding

See Also:
  nb help bookmark
  nb help browse
  nb help delete
  nb help edit
  nb help folders
  nb help import
  nb help show
  nb help todo

Examples:
  nb add
  nb add example.md
  nb add "Note content."
  nb add example.md --title "Example Title" --content "Example content."
  echo "Note content." | nb add
  nb add -t "Secret Document" --encrypt
  nb add example/document.md
  nb add folder sample/demo
  nb example:add
  nb example:add -t "Title"
  nb a
  nb a "Note content."
  nb example:a
  nb example:a -t "Title"

Aliases:
  nb create
  nb new

Shortcut Aliases:
  nb a
  nb +
```

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb bookmark [<ls-options>...]
  nb bookmark [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/] <url>
              [-c <comment> | --comment <comment>] [--edit] [-e | --encrypt]
              [-f <filename> | --filename <filename>] [--no-request]
              [-q <quote> | --quote <quote>] [--save-source]
              [-r (<url> | <selector>) | --related (<url> | <selector>)]...
              [-t <tag1>,<tag2>... | --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...] [--title <title>]

  nb bookmark (edit | delete | open | peek | url)
              ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
  nb bookmark search <query>

Options:
  -c, --comment <comment>      A comment or description for this bookmark.
  --edit                       Open the bookmark in your editor before saving.
  -e, --encrypt                Encrypt the bookmark with a password.
  -f, --filename <filename>    The filename for the bookmark. It is
                               recommended to omit the extension so the
                               default bookmark extension is used.
  --no-request                 Don't request or download the target page.
  -q, --quote <quote>          A quote or excerpt from the saved page.
                               Alias: `--excerpt`
  -r, --related <selector>     A selector for an item related to the
                               bookmarked page.
  -r, --related <url>          A URL for a page related to the bookmarked page.
                               Multiple `--related` flags can be used in a
                               command to save multiple related URLs.
  --save-source                Save the page source as HTML.
  -t, --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...  A comma-separated list of tags.
  --title <title>              The bookmark title. When not specified,
                               `nb` will use the html <title> tag.

Subcommands:
  (default)  Add a new bookmark for <url>, or list bookmarks.
             Bookmarks can also be added with `nb <url>`
  delete     Delete a bookmark.
  edit       Edit a bookmark.
  list       List bookmarks in the current notebook.
             Shortcut Alias: `ls`
  open       Open the bookmarked page in your system's primary web browser.
             Shortcut Alias: `o`
  peek       Open the bookmarked page in your terminal web browser.
             Alias: `preview`
             Shortcut Alias: `p`
  search     Search bookmarks for <query>.
             Shortcut Alias: `q`
  url        Print the URL for the specified bookmark.

Description:
  Create, view, search, edit, and delete bookmarks.

  By default, the html page content is saved within the bookmark, making the
  bookmarked page available for full-text search. When Pandoc [1] is
  installed, the HTML content is converted to Markdown before saving.
  When readability-cli [2] is install, markup is cleaned up to focus on
  content.

  `peek` opens the page in `w3m` [3] or `links` [4] when available.
  To specify a preferred browser, set the `$BROWSER` environment variable
  in your .bashrc, .zshrc, or equivalent, e.g.: export BROWSER="lynx"

  Bookmarks are identified by the `.bookmark.md` file extension. The
  bookmark URL is the first URL in the file within "<" and ">" characters:

    <https://www.example.com>

    1. https://pandoc.org/
    2. https://gitlab.com/gardenappl/readability-cli
    3. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m
    4. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)

Read More:

See Also:

  nb help open
  nb help peek
  nb help show
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#browse){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="browse"} `browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Browsing](#-browsing), [Images](#-images), [Linking](#-linking), [`add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete), [`edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#edit), [`list`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#list), [`ls`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#ls), [`open`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#open), [`peek`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#peek), [`pin`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#pin), [`search`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#search), [`show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show)

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb browse [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>]
            [-g | --gui] [-n | --notebooks] [-p | --print] [-q | --query <query>]
            [-s | --serve] [-t <tag> | --tag <tag> | --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...]
  nb browse add [<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<filename>]
            [-c <content> | --content <content>] [--tags <tag1>,<tag2>...]
            [-t <title> | --title <title>]
  nb browse delete ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
  nb browse edit ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])

Subcommands:
  (default)  Open a notebook, folder, or item in the terminal or GUI web browser.
  add        Open the add view in the browser.
             Shortcut Aliases: `a`, `+`
  delete     Open the delete view in the browser.
             Shortcut Aliases: `d`, `-`
  edit       Open the edit view in the browser.
             Shortcut Alias:   `e`

Options:
  -c, --content <content>      Add content to the new note.
  -g, --gui                    Open in the system's primary GUI web browser.
  -n, --notebooks              Browse notebooks.
  -p, --print                  Print to standard output.
  -q, --query <query>          Open to the search results for <query>.
  -s, --serve                  Start the web application server.
  -t, --tag <tag>              Search for a tag.
  --tags <tag1>,<tag2>...      A comma-separated list of tags.
  -t, --title <title>          Add a title to the new note.

Description:
  Browse, view, and edit linked notes, bookmarks, notebooks, folders, and
  other items using terminal and GUI web browsers.

  `browse` includes an embedded web application designed for terminal
  and GUI web browsers that renders [[wiki-style links]] and #tags as
  internal links, providing the ability to browse notes and notebooks,
  as well as seamlessly browse to and from the offsite links in
  bookmarks and notes.

  To link to a note or bookmark from another, include the selector for the
  target item within double square brackets anywhere in the linking document:

    # link to item 123 in the "sample" folder in the "example" notebook
    [[example:sample/123]]

    # link to the item titled "Example Title" in the "demo" notebook
    [[demo:Example Title]]

  `browse` supports `w3m` [1] and `links` [2], and depends on
  `ncat` [3] and `pandoc` [4]:

    1. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W3m
    2. https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Links_(web_browser)
    3. https://nmap.org/ncat/
    4. https://pandoc.org/

Read More:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb#-browsing

See Also:
  nb help add
  nb help delete
  nb help edit
  nb help list
  nb help ls
  nb help open
  nb help peek
  nb help pin
  nb help search
  nb help show
  nb help unpin

Examples:
  nb browse
  nb browse example:
  nb browse Example\ Folder/
  nb browse 123
  nb browse demo:456
  nb br

Shortcut Alias:
  nb b
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#do){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="do"} `do`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Todos](#-todos), [Tasks](#%EF%B8%8F-tasks), [`tasks`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#tasks), [`todo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#todo), [`undo`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#undo)

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#edit){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="edit"} `edit`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Editing](#editing), [`add`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#add), [`browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), [`delete`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#delete), [`move`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#move), [`show`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#show)

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb edit ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
          [-c <content> | --content <content>] [--edit]
          [-e <editor> | --editor <editor>] [--overwrite] [--prepend]

Options:
  -c, --content <content>  Content to add to the item.
  --edit                   Open the note in the editor before saving when
                           content is piped or passed as an argument.
  -e, --editor <editor>    Edit the note with <editor>, overriding the editor
                           specified in the `$EDITOR` environment variable.
  --overwrite              Overwrite existing content with <content> and
                           standard input.
  --prepend                Prepend <content> and standard input before
                           existing content.

Description:
  Open the specified note in `$EDITOR` or <editor> if specified.
  Content piped to `nb edit` or passed using the `--content` option
  is appended to the file without opening it in the editor,
  unless the `--edit` flag is specified.

  Non-text files are opened in your system's preferred app or program for
  that file type.

Read More:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb#editing

See Also:
  nb help add
  nb help browse
  nb help delete
  nb help move
  nb help show

Examples:
  nb edit 3
  nb edit example.md
  nb edit "A Document Title"
  echo "Content to append." | nb edit 1
  nb 3 edit
  nb example:edit 12
  nb edit example:12
  nb example:12 edit
  nb e 3
  nb 3 e
  nb e example:12
  nb example:12 e

Shortcut Alias:
  nb e
```

#### [![](data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB2aWV3Ym94PSIwIDAgMTYgMTYiIGFyaWEtaGlkZGVuPSJ0cnVlIj48dXNlIHhsaW5rOmhyZWY9IiNzdmctbGluayIgLz48L3N2Zz4=)](#export){.anchor-heading aria-labelledby="export"} `export`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}

[â†‘](#-help) Â· See also: [Import / Export](#%EF%B8%8F-import--export), [`browse`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#browse), [`import`{.language-plaintext .highlighter-rouge}](#import)

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb export ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
            <path> [-f | --force] [<pandoc options>...]
  nb export notebook <name> [<path>]
  nb export pandoc ([<notebook>:][<folder-path>/][<id> | <filename> | <title>])
            [<pandoc options>...]

Options:
  -f, --force   Skip the confirmation prompt when overwriting an existing file.

Subcommands:
  (default)     Export a file to <path>. If <path> has a different extension
                than the source note, convert the note using `pandoc`.
  notebook      Export the notebook <name> to the current directory or <path>.
                Alias for `nb notebooks export`.
  pandoc        Export the file to standard output or a file using `pandoc`.
                `export pandoc` prints to standard output by default.

Description:
  Export a file or notebook.

  If Pandoc [1] is available, convert the note from its current format
  to the format of the output file as indicated by the file extension
  in <path>. Any additional arguments are passed directly to Pandoc.
  See the Pandoc help information for available options.

    1. https://pandoc.org/

Read More:
  https://github.com/xwmx/nb#%EF%B8%8F-import--export

See Also:
  nb help browse
  nb help import

Examples:
  # Export an Org note
  nb export example.org /path/to/example.org

  # Export a Markdown note to HTML and print to standard output
  nb export pandoc example.md --from=markdown_strict --to=html

  # Export a Markdown note to a .docx Microsoft Office Word document
  nb export example.md /path/to/example.docx

  # Export note 12 in the "sample" notebook to HTML
  nb export sample:12 /path/to/example.html
```

``` highlight
Usage:
  nb init [<remote-url> [<branch>]] [--author] [--email <email>]
          [--name <name>]

Options:
  --author         Display the local email and name config prompt.
```
